| Optional / Follow-up | B8\~B13 | timeout, retry, idempotency, response shape, observability, cost source | If time remains or engineering-internal decision | [§6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.s7bybr323135) | discuss/defer |

3\. Track A — Required Product Decisions  
Audience: PM / Photo Review PM / Growth-Engagement / Design.

These 5 decisions must close before [§5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.v7w1qmlfbg0z) (Engineering). If they remain open, SOUP/MGAI have to assume the contract and storage shape, and the cost of changing them post-launch grows.  
3.1 A1+A3 — When do users see new coaching  
Severity: P0

What we're deciding. When a user who has received Photo Review changes a photo or profile, when should new coaching appear (same day / next day), and when a user opens the app the next day without changing any photo, which coaching should they see (yesterday's coaching / a freshly generated one). Once these two product questions are answered, the backend's storage shape and call frequency follow automatically. As a side decision, we also need to choose what to show during the gap between a photo change and the next-day new coaching (previous coaching as-is / a "we'll let you know soon" notice / empty state).

Recommendation.

- Q1 \= next day. Do not show new coaching the same day. This is consistent with PM view. Multiple new coachings on the same day fatigue the user and amplify the "change a photo → change another photo" pressure.  
- Q2 \= keep the same coaching. If the profile photo has not changed, there is no reason for the coaching content to differ. Generating fresh coaching every time creates inconsistency where the same user sees different coachings, and burns cost for no value.

The two answers combine into a one-line behavior:

New coaching the next day when the profile changes; otherwise keep the prior coaching.

User-perspective scenario.

- Monday morning: receives first coaching.  
- Monday afternoon: adds a photo. → No new coaching same day (prior Monday coaching kept, or empty state, per Q3).  
- Tuesday morning: new coaching (reflecting the changed photos).  
- Wednesday morning: no photo change. → Sees Tuesday's coaching as-is.  
- Thursday onward: no photo change. → Continues to see Tuesday's coaching.

Confirmed by source. Engineering Docs [§3.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) ([Photo Review MVP Engineering Docs](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U)): "A user triggers exactly one Photo Review call per day, and only if one of the following conditions is met: (1) First login after launch (cold start) — The user has never received a Photo Review. (2) Profile change — After their initial score, a returning user triggers a new call only when they change their profile (add/delete a photo, change bio, change prompt, add/delete an interest or descriptor)." This matches the Q1+Q2 recommendation in this doc exactly.

Exact definition of profile change (Engineering Docs [§3.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg)):

- photo add / delete  
- bio change  
- prompt change  
- interest add / delete  
- descriptor add / delete

This set must map 1:1 to the [§5.5 B6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.r1xgqe953h07) profile\_version increment trigger.

Risk if not decided.

- "Same-day new coaching" raises both user burden and cost.  
- "Generate fresh coaching daily even without profile change" makes the same user see different coachings, eroding product trust.  
- If the two answers stay ambiguous, backend cannot lock storage shape or call frequency.

Why this matters in this session. If "when does the user receive new coaching" is not frozen on the product side, backend has to proceed on assumed storage / call frequency / cache invalidation rules. Once launched, the meaning of storage is hard to change, so deciding here is the cheapest path.

Question for the room (product level only).

1. Q1: For a user who changes a photo the same day, is it better to surface new coaching the same day, or the next day?  
   1. Next day  
2. Q2: For a user whose photo/profile has not changed, how many days is it acceptable to keep showing the same coaching? (forever / refresh after some period / other)  
   1. Forever until dismissal or feature removal  
3. Q3: Right after a photo change and before the next-day new coaching arrives, what do we show? Previous coaching? "New coaching coming soon" notice? Empty state?  
   1. Some sort of celebratory & new coaching coming soon message \-\> will align with design for this screen

Agreement (fill in during meeting).

- Q1 (same day / next day): Next day  
- Q2 (keep / refresh after N days): Keep  
- Q3 (previous coaching / notice / empty state): Notice  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

Engineering note (PM may skip). If the answers settle on next day \+ profile\_version-based retention, SOUP implements (a) a "different calendar day from last generation" check and (b) a profile\_version-keyed cache. A 30-day hard ceiling is enough from a retention standpoint. See [§5.6 B7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.g9cgep2lrbzv) for implementation detail.  
3.2 A2 — Coaching surface exposure model \+ LLM output definition  
Severity: P0 (response schema and surface exposure policy affect client/SOUP/AURA)

What we're deciding. The latest Figma already includes the coach information shown on the bottom sheet and the Edit Photos screen. However, per Evan/Jaini's 2026-04-24\~25 agreement, the bottom sheet appears only at the next app open, not in the same session — within the same session, coaching appears only on persistent surfaces (Profile Home, Edit Photos, Photo Cropper). On top of that, this slot closes 4 operational decisions — (i) which visible elements the backend response returns in a single call and in what shape, (ii) how to present a repetitive photo cluster to the user, (iii) whether AURA should derive additional non-visible signals (e.g., status="skip"), and (iv) which images to use under the bottom sheet and how many insights to expose to a single user at once.

Surface exposure model in one line (Evan \+ Jaini agreement, 2026-04-24\~25):

- Day N (the session in which coaching is generated): shown only on persistent surfaces (Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper). Do not interrupt while the user is swiping.  
- Day N+1 onward (next app open): bottom sheet appears as a nudge. Tapping it opens the Edit Photos screen.  
- Reference quotes: Evan (4/24): "Why do we need to nudge the user in the same session we trigger coaching generation for option 2? ... It should be feasible to save state that is read on next app open giving an experience similar to option 1." / Jaini (4/25): "once the coaching is ready, it shows up in the persistent surface areas (i.e. profile home, edit photos, photo cropper) and then at next app open is when the bottom sheet could show up."

This decision splits into 4 topics. The meeting follows the same order.

| Sub-section | Topic | Decision form |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| [3.2.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.6ip59ri0fi4n) | Backend 6-element mapping | freeze |
| [3.2.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.40bkz0jhc7gi) | Repetitive photo handling model | choose 1 of 4 |
| [3.2.3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.m5tvplya6ieb) | AURA-derived additional signals (skip / severity, etc.) | discuss \+ select |
| [3.2.4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.2cphljq6gksq) | Bottom sheet UX (image approach / content / max insights) | discuss \+ decide |

The operational rules sit on top of the 4 sub-section decisions.

- Day N (the session in which coaching is generated): do not show the bottom sheet. If the user enters Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper, coaching appears there. If the user does not enter those surfaces, no coaching appears in that session.  
- Day N+1 onward (next app open): for users whose cache has a ready coaching they have not yet viewed, the bottom sheet appears as a nudge at app open. Once dismissed, eligibility is removed per [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm).  
- Bottom sheet metrics map to the bottom\_sheet\_\* category in [§6.3 A10](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.j607oxyxzrxc).

Engineering note (PM may skip). Verifying that AURA can stably produce all elements in one call within prompt/token limits, and the path for sending the ready signal to the client (push/polling), are covered in [§5.1 B1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.utdhzivpsb7i), [§6.4 B8](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.1tvn8h51l6g3), and [§6.8 B12](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.y5pw05f1itk).  
3.2.1 Backend response — 6 visible elements mapping  
What we're deciding. Figma shows the user 4 visible copy elements (bottom sheet title/body, and coach title/body on the Edit Photos screen after click-through) and 2 photo-level pieces of information (which photos are problematic and why). We decide which field names and which shape the backend uses to return these 6 elements in a single call. We also close whether to keep ⑤ problematic photo id list and ⑥ per-photo problem descriptions separate or combine them, since they are essentially the same data in two shapes.

Figma flow and the 6 elements.

```
[App open]
   └─ ready state → bottom sheet appears
       ├─ ① bottom_sheet_title          (one-line title)
       └─ ② bottom_sheet_body            (benefit copy, "why look")
           ├─ "Review" tap →
           └─ Edit Photos screen
               ├─ ③ coach_title          (one-line problem title)
               ├─ ④ coach_body            (suggested action body)
               ├─ ⑤ problematic_photo_ids (which photos are problematic, references request photo id)
               └─ ⑥ per_photo_problems   (per-photo problem description)
```

These 6 are outputs of the same generation, so the AURA response returns them together in one call.

| Element | Candidate field name | Shape | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| ① bottom sheet title | bottom\_sheet\_title | string | one-line attention copy |
| ② bottom sheet body | bottom\_sheet\_body | string | benefit copy |
| ③ coach title | coach\_title | string | problem title on Edit Photos screen |
| ④ coach body | coach\_body | string | suggested action detail |
| ⑤ problematic photo ids | problematic\_photo\_ids | string\[\] | references request photos\[\].id |
| ⑥ per-photo problem | per\_photo\_problems | array of {photo\_id, problem\_description} | rationale for each photo in ⑤ |

⑤ and ⑥ are essentially one piece of data viewed in two shapes.

Recommendation.

- Freeze the 6 elements above as-is (1:1 with Figma).  
- Start with ⑤+⑥ as a combined model (per\_photo\_problems only). If the client needs the photo\_id list, it can extract it from the array. Splitting them duplicates the same information in two places and creates consistency risk.

Sample (combined model).

```json
"per_photo_problems": [
  {"photo_id": "abc-123", "problem_description": "The strong filter makes face recognition difficult"},
  {"photo_id": "def-456", "problem_description": "Angle/style is similar to other photos, lacks variety"}
]
```

Risk if not decided.

- If Figma elements and backend fields don't map 1:1, client mapping wobbles right before launch.  
- ⑥ per-photo descriptions grow with the photo count, which can pull token-limit issues along.

Question for the room.

- Q1.1: Do the 6 elements above match Figma's information structure?  
- Q1.2: Split ⑤+⑥, or combine into per\_photo\_problems only? (Recommendation: combine)

Agreement.

- Freeze 6-element mapping (Yes / change): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Handling of ⑤ \+ ⑥ (split / combine): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

3.2.2 Repetitive photo handling model  
What we're deciding. When a user's profile contains a repetitive cluster of similar photos, how do we present it to the user? Mark every photo in the cluster equally, focus on one cluster at a time, or highlight only the worst photo in the cluster — the model we pick determines whether the backend has to produce separate cluster grouping or ranking information.

Four models are possible: prior behavior, current Figma, Nancy's proposal (2026-04-08 Slack), and a worst-highlight variant.

| Model | Behavior | Required LLM output |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| (Prior) Best-keep | Don't mark the best photo in the cluster; mark the rest as "duplicate" | per-photo flag (achievable with current 6 elements) |
| (Current Figma) Mark-all | Mark all repetitive photos in the cluster at the same depth | per-photo flag (achievable with current 6 elements) |
| (Nancy proposal) One-cluster-at-a-time | Show only one cluster at a time; once resolved, surface the next cluster on the next visit | cluster grouping info needed (repetitive\_clusters or cluster\_id) |
| Worst-highlight | Strongly highlight the worst photo in a cluster; soft-mark the rest | repetitive\_clusters or per-photo rank\_in\_cluster |

Nancy quote (Photo Review Slack, 2026-04-08): "we could only show 1 repetitive issue at a time ... the rationale is bc the copy on the profile home module is so tied to the edit profile one, that it feels like we'd have to keep the user focused on one photo issue at a time."

Choosing one-cluster-at-a-time or worst-highlight requires extra cluster or ranking information in the backend. Two element shapes:

```json
"repetitive_clusters": [
  {
    "cluster_id": "c1",
    "photo_ids_ranked_worst_first": ["def-456", "abc-123"]
  }
]
```

Or inline cluster\_id \+ rank\_in\_cluster in per\_photo\_problems:

```json
"per_photo_problems": [
  {"photo_id": "def-456", "problem_description": "...", "cluster_id": "c1", "rank_in_cluster": 1},
  {"photo_id": "abc-123", "problem_description": "...", "cluster_id": "c1", "rank_in_cluster": 2}
]
```

Recommendation.

- Handling model is One-cluster-at-a-time (Nancy's proposal). Letting users focus on one issue at a time and surfacing the next cluster on the next visit best balances copy convenience with user burden. The same data can also support worst-highlight, leaving room for future extension.  
- Cluster information shape: inline cluster\_id \+ rank\_in\_cluster inside per\_photo\_problems. A separate field would force the client to join two arrays and increase mapping code.

Question for the room.

- Q2.1: Of the 4 models, which matches product intent? (Recommendation: One-cluster-at-a-time)  
- Q2.2: If a model needs additional elements, put cluster info in a separate field, or inline it in per\_photo\_problems? (Recommendation: inline)

Agreement.

- Handling model (Best-keep / Mark-all / One-cluster-at-a-time / Worst-highlight): One-cluster-at-a-time but still needs to not mark the best photo in the cluster  
- Cluster info shape (separate field / inline / N/A): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

3.2.3 Additional signals AURA should derive  
Some signals can only be decided on the LLM side. Beyond the 6 elements visible to the user, this section explicitly agrees what additional signals AURA should derive and return to backend.

| Topic | Candidate element | Derivable only by LLM | Decision impact |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Eligibility skip signal | status (success/skip) \+ skip\_reason | Yes | Direct link to the two-stage gate in [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) |
| Repetitive cluster info | repetitive\_clusters or rank\_in\_cluster | Yes | Determined by the model picked in [3.2.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.40bkz0jhc7gi) |
| Problem severity | severity (low/med/high) per photo | Yes | Priority sort, UI accent decisions |
| Priority photo recommendation | recommended\_swap\_photo | Yes | Clearer guidance / increases prompt complexity |
| Overall evaluation score | overall\_score or confidence | Yes | Enables A/B analysis / threshold filter |
| Suggested next action clarity | cta\_label | Partial (LLM or product copy table) | Client can use button copy directly |
| Localization handling | locale meta or localized copy vs key | No (engineering decision) | Splits client vs backend handling |

Recommendation.

- Adopt status (success/skip) \+ skip\_reason — required to make the [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) Stage 2 LLM gate work.  
- Repetitive cluster info is auto-adopted based on the [§3.2.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.40bkz0jhc7gi) recommendation (One-cluster-at-a-time).  
- All other signals (severity, recommended\_swap\_photo, overall\_score, cta\_label, locale) are excluded from MVP and follow-up. Reason: there is no Figma slot for them, adding them inflates prompt complexity and token cost, and adding them once post-launch data justifies them is the safer path.

Question for the room.

- Q3.1: Do we adopt the behavior where AURA's LLM judges "this user is already diverse / non-repetitive" and returns status="skip"? (Recommendation: Yes)  
- Q3.2: Are there any other LLM-derived signals from the table above we should include in MVP? (Recommendation: none, follow-up)

Agreement.

- Adopt LLM-derived skip signal (Yes / No): YES  
- Additional LLM-derived element to include (none / \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_): None in MVP  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

3.2.4 Bottom sheet UX (Spec Kick-off new)  
What we're deciding. Bottom sheet exposure timing was decided in [§3.2 What we're deciding](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) as next app open. This sub-section settles the UX details on top of that — what kind of image to show under the bottom sheet, whether to use one image as a catch-all for both add CTA and replace CTA or to split them, and how many insights to expose to a single user at once.

We group the UX items posted in today's Spec Kick-off [Notes](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1VxtA1qjkyZshECqtrLOL7NDe5G8CJiV6Mltmm6HHurw).

(a) Bottom sheet image approach (proposed by Nancy Wu):

- Option 1 — catch-all: one image covers both add CTA and replace CTA.  
- Option 2 — split: separate images for add and replace.

(b) Which image to show on the bottom sheet: the latest Figma fans out 3 photos like a card-game hand. Which photos go there is a separate decision.

| Candidate | Tone | Trade-off |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| User's own problematic photos | "look at these photos" | Strong directness. Self-criticism exposure burden |
| User's own best photos | "let's grow more of this" | Light burden. Indirect about what the problem is |
| User's photos fan-out (current Figma) | Neutral | Needs ranking signal for which photos to put in the fan |
| Stock/illustration | Safe | Cannot express add/replace tone difference |
| Hybrid (Add=stock, Replace=problematic) | Tone-splittable | Combined with (a) Option 2 |

(c) Max insights per user: the Spec Kick-off body says "no cap needed for MVP?". MVP looks like it's leaning to no cap.

Recommendation.

- (a) Image approach \= Option 2 (split). The tones of add CTA and replace CTA are fundamentally different (encouragement to add vs guidance to replace), so a catch-all dulls one of them.  
- (b) Image content \= Hybrid (stock/illustration for Add, problematic photos for Replace). Add targets users without enough photos to display, so stock fits naturally; for Replace, directly showing the problematic photo is the most effective behavior trigger.  
- (c) Max insights cap \= no cap in MVP. Add a cap post-launch if user fatigue indicators (viewed/dismissed ratio, session length change) show the need.

Question for the room.

- Q4.1: Bottom sheet image approach — catch-all (Option 1\) or split add vs replace (Option 2)? (Recommendation: Option 2\)  
- Q4.2: Image content on the bottom sheet — problematic / best / fan-out / stock / hybrid? (Recommendation: Hybrid)  
- Q4.3: If using user photos, by what criteria do we pick them? (problematic priority, best ranking, or delegate to LLM)  
- Q4.4: Max insights cap — go with no cap for MVP? (Recommendation: no cap)

Agreement.

- Image approach (catch-all / split): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Image content (problematic / best / fan-out / stock / hybrid): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Image selection criteria (when using user photos): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Max insights cap (none / number): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

3.3 A4 — Which users do we not show coaching to  
Severity: P0

What we're deciding. The reason "Option 2 \= coaching on every app open unconditionally" does not apply is precisely this skip rule. If the rule isn't clear, the same user gets repeated coaching, fatigue piles up, cost balloons, and we end up with an incident post-launch. We need to lock who is excluded and where the exclusion gets evaluated.

Recommendation.

- Why now. This is Stage 1 input into [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915). If product does not freeze the skip set, SOUP's gate code can't be written and AURA can't decide what to put behind status="skip".

Recommendation (skip targets).

The following users get no new coaching. The judgement happens in two places — conditions decidable from input data alone are owned by SOUP, and conditions that need to look at the photos themselves go to AURA (LLM) (see [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915)).

- (SOUP) User received coaching recently and photos/profile have not changed since (per [§3.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) Q2, keep the same coaching)  
- (SOUP) User changed photo/profile the same day (per [§3.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) Q1, new coaching the next day)  
- (SOUP) User is policy-ineligible due to experiment, region, privacy, age, etc.  
- (SOUP) Profile-restriction geo or photo count \< 4 (Confluence spec: "We will avoid profile restrictions geos for this experiment")  
- (SOUP) User has dismissed per [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm)  
- (AURA / LLM) User whose photos are sufficiently diverse and non-repetitive that LLM judges no coaching is needed — the Hybrid (high diversity / low repetitiveness) definition already exists on the product side, so we put the criteria in the prompt and the LLM evaluates.

Eligibility segments specified in the Confluence WIP spec ([WIP Photo Review & Feedback](https://gotinder.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SOUP/pages/1898905601), updated 2026-04-24):

| Segment | Audience | MVP coaching |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Segment 1 | 6+ photos & low/medium diversity | Yes |
| Segment 2 | \< 6 photos (diversity irrelevant) | Yes |
| Skip (LLM judgment) | 6+ photos & high diversity | No (LLM returns status="skip") |
| Skip (SOUP) | profile-restriction geo / \< 4 photos | No (out of this experiment) |

Risk if not decided.

- The same user unintentionally receives repeated coaching, accumulating fatigue.  
- Even with post-launch data, product cannot consistently explain "why this user got coaching."

Why this matters in this session. SOUP must implement the deterministic gate from this set. If the set isn't frozen, SOUP can't start mock or integration. AURA also can't define what status="skip" covers without Stage 1 settled.

Question for the room (product level only).

1. Do we agree to use the five skip target sets above as the baseline as-is?  
2. Are new users (first app open, low photo count) skip targets, or immediate coaching targets?  
3. For product consistency, should users who opted out of other nudges/features be auto-skipped here?

Agreement (fill in during meeting).

- Freeze 5 skip targets (Yes / change): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- New user handling: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Other-nudge opt-out user handling: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

3.4 A5 — When do we generate coaching, and where does it appear  
Severity: P0 (mostly confirm — PM agreement already exists)

What we're deciding. Among PMs, the agreement "generate at app open for every eligible user" already exists. We need to verify it once more in this slot. Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper are surfaces that display an already-generated result, not generation points. We also confirm whether deep-link entries (notification → app entry) follow the same model.

Recommendation.

- New coaching is generated only at app open.  
- Profile Home, Edit Photos, Photo Cropper entries serve only as result display surfaces.  
- Even if the same user opens the app multiple times the same day, no further new coaching is generated per [§3.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db).

Risk if not decided.

- If multiple entry points generate, the same user creates several coachings in a short time, raising user burden and cost.  
- If PM agreement is not verified, post-launch we get questions like "why doesn't X screen produce a fresh one?"

Why this matters in this session. "Verify PM agreement" sounds light but it locks SOUP's call model and cost estimate baseline. If we leave it open, both shake.

Question for the room (product level only).

1. Do all PMs agree on "new coaching only at app open; other screens are display surfaces"?  
2. What product signal would make us add Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper entry as a new coaching trigger later? (e.g., revisit if app-open conversion is low)  
3. Do deep-link cases (notification → app entry) get treated the same as a regular app open?

3.5 A6 — What happens after a user dismisses  
Severity: P0

What we're deciding. What is the product meaning of the user action "dismiss"? Specifically, after a user dismisses Photo Review's coaching, do they ever see it again? If so, under what conditions? Without an answer, users react negatively ("why again?") and backend has no idea whether to keep generating for them.

PM-side question (product level).

If a user dismisses Photo Review coaching, will they see coaching again afterward? If yes, under what conditions?

Recommendation.

- Treat dismiss as a strong signal of "I no longer want this feature." The user no longer receives coaching after dismiss.  
- A "re-invitation" campaign (a separate product decision) can later make them eligible again — that entry point is follow-up.  
- Even if the user adds new photos, we do not auto-resume. Respect the user's dismiss intent first.

The summary in one line:

Dismiss is final. Without an explicit separate decision, no further coaching is shown.

Risk if not decided.

- "Show again after a short time" makes the user dismiss again, accumulating negative reactions.  
- Conversely, "show again if photos change after dismiss" contradicts the user's intended opt-out.

Why this matters in this session. Dismiss semantics drive both [§5.4 B5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.rk2a2g52g598) (dismissed\_at field) and the Stage 1 condition in [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915). If product leaves it open, both sides have to assume.

Question for the room (product level only).

1. Is "dismiss \= no more coaching" the right behavior, or should we re-show under some conditions?  
2. If the user adds/changes photos, should dismiss auto-clear? (Recommendation: do not clear)  
3. If a re-invitation campaign becomes likely, who brings that decision and when?

Agreement (fill in during meeting).

- Dismiss \= no more coaching afterward (Yes / other behavior): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Dismiss auto-clear on profile change (No / Yes / conditional): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Future re-invitation campaign owner / criteria: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

There is little Track B → Track A flow. Product decisions go first; engineering takes those inputs and locks the contract.  
5\. Track B — Required Engineering Decisions  
Audience: SOUP backend, AURA/MGAI engineers, Client/Surface engineering.

Take [§3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.15m0x797spk8)'s inputs as-is and freeze the contract and implementation boundary. Once these 6 items close, both sides can start mock/integration.  
5.1 B1 — SOUP → AURA single endpoint  
Severity: P0 (the zero point of engineering work)

What we're deciding. What endpoint surface SOUP and AURA agree on so that both teams can begin parallel implementation. Specifically, whether to freeze a single POST /v1/photo-review and keep AURA stateless, vs. building auxiliary status/result/cancel endpoints. We also decide where read/state contracts live (inside SOUP, or on a client-facing API).

Recommendation.

- Endpoint freezes as POST /v1/photo-review only.  
- AURA remains a stateless generation service. We do not build product-state endpoints like status / result / cancel / dismiss / viewed.  
- Read/state contracts for displaying results to the user or surfacing them in the next session are handled inside SOUP or by a client-facing API.

API surface organized by layer:

| Layer | API | Required | Owner | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| SOUP → AURA | POST /v1/photo-review | Required | AURA/MGAI | Frozen in this session |
| SOUP internal | profile\_version-keyed result store/lookup | Required | SOUP | Invalidate on profile change, hard ceiling 30 days |
| Client → SOUP | Coaching state included in Profile Home / Edit Photos response | Required | SOUP / Client | Extend existing API or new endpoint |
| Client → SOUP | viewed / dismissed / clicked marking | Required | SOUP / Client | Product state \+ analytics |
| SOUP → AURA | GET /v1/photo-review/{id} | Not built | — | Only needed if AURA becomes an async job service |
| SOUP → AURA | cancel / delete | Not built | — | Unnecessary if AURA does not store results |

Risk if not decided.

- SOUP cannot start mock or integration work.  
- AURA cannot lock request validation and response schema.  
- Contract mismatches surface in QA/E2E right before launch.

Why this matters in this session. SOUP and AURA need to run parallel implementation. If contract isn't frozen, both have to assume — and contract mismatches found late are the most expensive.

Question for the room.

1. Can SOUP start mock/integration on the POST /v1/photo-review contract immediately?  
2. Do you agree to the boundary that AURA provides only a stateless generation API?  
3. Where do the read/state APIs live — inside SOUP, or on a client-facing API — and who is the owner?

Agreement (fill in during meeting).

- Freeze single endpoint (Yes / change): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Agree AURA stateless (Yes / No): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Read/state API owner: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

5.2 B2 \+ B3 — P0 fields and photo path format  
Severity: P0 (mock/contract dependency)

What we're deciding. Which P0 required fields the SOUP → AURA contract carries, and which single photo S3 reference format is used. Without these, SOUP doesn't know what data to gather, AURA can't write request validation, and accepting two photo formats creates subtle drift across client/SOUP/AURA.

Recommendation.

P0 required fields:

| Field | Required | Reason |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| request\_id | Yes | tracing, idempotency, debugging |
| age | Yes | segment matching, prompt context |
| gender | Yes | segment matching, prompt context |
| country\_code | Yes | ISO 3166-1 alpha-2, e.g., US, KR |
| interests | Yes | personalized photo suggestion |
| bio | Yes | coaching behavior depends on whether bio exists |
| photos | Yes | primary input |
| photos\[\].id | Yes | response photo reference, repetitive identification |
| photos\[\].bucket | Yes | S3 image loading |
| photos\[\].s3\_key | Yes | S3 image loading |
| profile\_version | Yes | freshness key. SOUP-owned ([B6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.fs5kg3p797yf)) |

Photo S3 reference format:

- Default: bucket \+ s3\_key. Do not accept both formats simultaneously.  
- If SOUP can more easily provide a full S3 path, unify the contract on full path only.

For P1 optional fields and naming policy, see [Appendix A](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.onhhl06qfu33).

Risk if not decided.

- Mock data drifts from real SOUP data, forcing rework at integration.  
- AURA assumes nullable policy and types and proceeds, with security/validation issues surfacing late.

Why this matters in this session. Mock work depends on the field set. We need it locked before SOUP and AURA can build in parallel.

Question for the room.

1. Can SOUP provide all 11 P0 required fields now, or are any new values needed?  
2. Which photo S3 reference is more natural for SOUP — bucket \+ s3\_key or full S3 path?  
3. Does any user have photos across multiple buckets?

- Freeze P0 fields (Yes / add/remove): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Photo path format: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Fields needing new build, with owner / due: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

5.3 B4 — SOUP owns the trigger gate  
Severity: P0 (where Track A decisions live as code)

What we're deciding. Where the gate that decides "do we call AURA?" lives, and how it splits between SOUP and AURA. The gate has two stages — (a) deterministic conditions decidable from input data alone, owned by SOUP, and (b) conditions that require LLM judgement on the actual photos (e.g., "are the photos diverse enough"), evaluated by AURA at inference time. Without this split, SOUP tries to imitate the LLM domain and the boundary breaks; AURA gets exposed to product state and responsibilities mix.

Recommendation — two-stage gate.

Stage 1: SOUP-side deterministic gate (judgeable from input data alone).

```
App open
  → SOUP: check experiment / region / feature-gate eligibility
  → SOUP: check dismissed_at ([§3.5 A6])
  → SOUP: check profile / photo change ([§5.5 B6] profile_version)
  → SOUP: check whether last generation date is a different calendar day from today ([§3.1 A1+A3])
  → Only when all conditions pass: SOUP → AURA POST /v1/photo-review
```

Stage 2: AURA-side LLM-derived gate (judgeable only by looking at the photos).

```
AURA receives POST /v1/photo-review
  → AURA: prompt + Gemini call (evaluate user photos)
  → LLM judgment: this user is already diverse / non-repetitive → status="skip", fill skip_reason
  → Otherwise: status="success" + 6-element coaching response
  → SOUP: store in cache or record generation_skipped event based on response status
```

So among the [§3.3 A4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.q4iaelimp80o) skip conditions, "high diversity / low repetitiveness" is judged by AURA, not SOUP. The rest is SOUP's call.

Risk if not decided.

- If SOUP imitates the LLM domain (diversity/repetition judgment), accuracy drops and product criteria scatter.  
- If AURA holds product state (dismiss, last-generated-date, etc.), deletion/retention responsibility flows into the inference layer.  
- Without a skip branch in the response, SOUP misreads "LLM-judged skip" as a normal success and stores wrongly in cache.  
- Mismatched timing between SOUP's deterministic gate and AURA endpoint availability slips launch.

Why this matters in this session. The two-stage gate is the place Track A decisions take code form. Without locking it, both teams keep guessing about boundary.

Question for the room.

1. Do SOUP/MGAI agree to the structure where AURA judges "this user is already diverse / non-repetitive" via LLM at inference time and returns status="skip"?  
2. Are there additional signals AURA should derive? (e.g., tie-breaker ranking, severity, repetitive cluster, recommended\_swap\_photo — see [§3.2 A2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) Open discussion table)  
3. Does SOUP already have profile/photo change detection, or does it need to be built?  
4. Is eligibility (deterministic part) a SOUP-internal service, or dependent on a separate service?  
5. Implementation timeline: how many days after [§3.3 A4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.q4iaelimp80o), [§3.4 A5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.upygd9ysc76a), [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm) decisions are SOUP-side and AURA-side gates each feasible?

Agreement (fill in during meeting).

- Agree two-stage gate (SOUP deterministic \+ AURA LLM-derived) (Yes / change): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Additional signals AURA must derive: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- profile/photo change detection availability: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- SOUP-side / AURA-side build due / owner: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

5.4 B5 — State ownership boundary  
Severity: P0 (core of data ownership and SOUP LOE)

What we're deciding. Which team owns which state — product state (viewed, dismissed\_at, last\_generated\_at, profile\_version, surface exposure, bottom sheet impression) vs. inference metadata (prompt/model versioning, inference logs, model latency/status). Without ownership, next-session UX, day-boundary check, dismissal, and duplicate prevention all wobble between teams, and SOUP's LOE estimate shifts heavily. AURA holding product state pulls deletion/retention/privacy into the inference layer and inflates long-term ownership cost.

Recommendation.

| Component | Owns |
| :---- | :---- |
| SOUP / Product backend | viewed, dismissed\_at, last\_generated\_at (= last generation date; new generation only allowed when today is a different calendar day), profile\_version or snapshot hash, cached coaching by profile\_version, surface exposure history, bottom sheet impression/dismiss state |
| AURA / MGAI | prompt/model versioning, inference request log, prompt version, model name/config, Gemini latency/status/error, inference output payload, short-lived inference cache (optional) |

Explicit dismiss handling. When dismissed\_at is set, the user is removed from the eligibility pool per [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm). It is a single flag independent of other timing conditions like day-boundary or profile\_version.

Risk if not decided.

- The ML system ends up holding product state, blurring the ownership boundary.  
- SOUP can't tell whether new storage is needed or extending existing storage suffices.

Why this matters in this session. Ownership feeds B7 Persistence storage choice and SOUP's LOE estimate. Without it locked, SOUP can't size the work.

Question for the room.

1. Can SOUP store all the product state above, or does some part need new storage?  
2. Does adopting dismissed\_at and last\_generated\_at conflict with existing user preferences systems?  
3. Is the minimal AURA-side metadata in the table enough?  
4. Where does the deletion/retention/privacy responsibility owner sit?

Agreement (fill in during meeting).

- Freeze state ownership table (Yes / change): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Any new SOUP storage needed: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- privacy/retention review owner: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

5.5 B6 — Profile freshness key  
Severity: P0 (shared ground for cache invalidation, dedupe, idempotency)

What we're deciding. What single value represents profile freshness — profile\_version vs. snapshot hash — and which fields trigger an increment. This single key is what makes "is this coaching valid for the current profile?" answerable, and without it the [§5.6 B7 cache](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.g9cgep2lrbzv) has no invalidation criterion.

Recommendation.

- Include SOUP-owned profile\_version (or an equivalent immutable profile snapshot hash) in the AURA request.  
- AURA uses this value only as part of the idempotency/cache key and never modifies it directly.  
- The increment trigger set maps 1:1 to the canonical definition in the [§3.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) Engineering Docs:  
  - photo add / delete  
  - bio change  
  - prompt change  
  - interest add / delete  
  - descriptor add / delete

(Photo reorder, core fields like age/gender/country, and relationship intent are not in the trigger set today. If needed, PM brings a separate decision.)

Risk if not decided.

- Stale coaching might be exposed against an updated profile.  
- No way to prevent duplicate generation against the same profile.  
- Even with a profile\_version-keyed cache, no invalidation criterion means stale results pile up.

Why this matters in this session. Profile key is shared infrastructure under [B7 cache](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.lli4m5ix9c6a) and [B10 dedupe](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.ifatdxju2440). If we leave it open, both wobble.

Question for the room.

1. Does SOUP already have a profile-version concept?  
2. Is a new concept or a snapshot hash faster to build for SOUP?  
3. What field scope goes into MVP freshness?

Agreement (fill in during meeting).

- Profile freshness key shape (profile\_version / snapshot hash / other): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Increment/hash input field set: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Build owner / due: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

5.6 B7 — Persistence: profile\_version-keyed cache  
Severity: P0 (UX vs. backend design fork)

What we're deciding. Cache shape, storage layer, and retention/legal review owner. Implementing the [§3.1 A1+A3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) product decision ("keep same coaching when photos do not change, new coaching next day when they do") directly produces a cache that is valid while profile\_version stays the same, not one that expires by time. We just need to lock the cache key shape, storage layer, and retention/legal review owner here.

Recommendation.

- Implement a profile\_version-keyed cache in SOUP. The same cache entry keeps getting reused as long as the profile is unchanged. Strict ephemeral is not adopted.  
- Cache key \= (user\_id, profile\_version, prompt\_version, model\_name). Same as the dedupe key ([§6.6 B10](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.b6k1csktdmh3)).  
- Hard ceiling starts at \~30 days as a retention/legal hypothesis. The ceiling is for storage hygiene, not invalidation.  
- Cache and exposure state are owned by SOUP / product backend ([§5.4 B5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.rk2a2g52g598)).  
- AURA response includes profile\_version (or hash), prompt\_version, and model\_name so SOUP can construct the cache key.  
- Single cache invalidation trigger: change in profile\_version. "No same-day new generation" is handled by the day-boundary check in generation ([§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915)), not by cache.  
- Storage layer candidates: existing SOUP redis / dynamodb / new store. Owner decides.

Risk if not decided.

- Without a storage candidate, SOUP's gap between mock and real implementation widens.  
- Retention/legal review landing right before launch is a schedule risk.

Why this matters in this session. The cache shape is the implementation form of A1+A3. With B6 freshness key in place, choosing the storage layer is the only remaining gate.

Question for the room.

1. What does SOUP implement the storage layer with (redis / dynamodb / other)?  
2. Add to the existing data model, or create a separate store?  
3. How far has retention/legal review progressed, and who owns the next round?

Agreement (fill in during meeting).

- Storage layer choice: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Existing vs. new store: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Retention/legal review owner / due: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

6\. Optional / Follow-up (if time remains)  
Once [§3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.15m0x797spk8) and [§5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.v7w1qmlfbg0z) close, SOUP and AURA can start mock/integration. The items below are (a) not launch-blocking, (b) decidable inside engineering, or (c) follow-up async. If time remains, close one or two; otherwise just set owner and due date.  
6.1 A7 — Stability of response key naming  
Context. Verify whether the [§3.2 A2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) backend response fields (bottom\_sheet\_title, bottom\_sheet\_body, coach\_title, coach\_body, per\_photo\_problems) remain stable post-launch.

Recommendation. If PM/Content guarantees that Figma copy/surface names won't shake for at least 6 months post-launch, use the field names above as-is. If stability is weak, start with generalized keys (hook\_title, hook\_body, coach\_title, coach\_body, photo\_problems) so the schema doesn't move with product copy. Owner: PM \+ Content, follow-up async.  
6.2 A9 — Tie-breaker metric  
Context. Who decides the representative photo within a repetitive photo cluster. Not an MVP blocker, but the tie-breaker should be consistent.

Recommendation. Hybrid — use a universal photo-quality metric when one exists, fall back to LLM visual judgment otherwise. Once metric coverage is wide enough, follow-up can unify it.  
6.3 A10 — Analytics event taxonomy  
Context. Tracking user behavior post-launch requires a frozen event taxonomy.

Recommendation. Freeze 5 categories (Generation lifecycle / Surface impression / Bottom sheet / Profile change / Failure-skip) as baseline. Per-category event details in the [Appendix Analytics](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.qzu97hagv42f). Attach 7 common dimensions (request\_id, user\_id, profile\_version, prompt\_version, model\_name, experiment\_arm, surface, session\_id) to every event. This session agrees only on the category structure; PM \+ Analytics close per-event additions/adjustments async.  
6.4 B8 — Timeout and late result  
Context. Gemini sync p99 is around 30.5 seconds, so timeouts happen even in normal operation.

Recommendation. SOUP→AURA timeout \= 30 seconds. Late results arriving after timeout flow into the [§5.6 B7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.g9cgep2lrbzv) cache and are used in the next surface/session. Timeout/failure are recorded as observability events. Detail in [Appendix F.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.o67513q9a6mf). Engineering can decide internally.  
6.5 B9 — Retry budget  
Context. Retry raises success rate but increases cost and latency together.

Recommendation. Single in-AURA transient retry within a 30-second budget. SOUP does not re-call the same request and keeps the idempotency key. Retry-induced cost is reported as a separate item in cost estimates. Detail in [Appendix F.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.5rhxxhtme801).  
6.6 B10 — Idempotency / dedupe  
Context. Handling tracing and dedupe with a single request\_id causes incidents where retry breaks dedupe.

Recommendation. Split the keys. request\_id is for tracing/idempotency only (issued by SOUP). generation\_key \= (user\_id, profile\_version, prompt\_version, model\_name) is for dedupe only. If an in-flight request exists with the same dedupe key, no new Gemini call is started; retries keep the same two keys. Detail in [Appendix F.3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.y4480sj9ljwm).  
6.7 B11 — Response shape  
Context. Final schema is closed by taking the [§3.2.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.6ip59ri0fi4n) Q1.2 (combined/split) and [§3.2.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.40bkz0jhc7gi) Q2.2 (cluster inline/separate) decisions.

Recommendation. Return the Figma 6 elements \+ skip branch in a single call:

- Always included: request\_id, status (success/skip), prompt\_name, prompt\_version, model\_name.  
- For status="success": bottom\_sheet\_title, bottom\_sheet\_body, coach\_title, coach\_body, per\_photo\_problems (+ inline cluster\_id / rank\_in\_cluster per Q2.2).  
- For status="skip": skip\_reason required, the 6 elements omitted.

Sample in [Appendix A.5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.ehozon1a1qok). Naming stability decided in [§6.1 A7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.c19rdsusi8hi).  
6.8 B12 — Observability  
Context. Product event taxonomy (A10) and backend metrics are separated.

Recommendation. Product events are the 5 categories frozen in [§6.3 A10](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.j607oxyxzrxc). Backend metrics: request count / success / timeout / failure (reason) / Gemini latency distribution (p50/p90/p95/p99) / token count (input/output) / prompt\_version / model\_name. Detail in [Appendix F.4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.co4wq0usvswn).  
6.9 B13 — Cost / latency source consistency  
Context. A comment noted that latency was measured on gemini-3.1-flash-lite-preview while cost's underlying model is unclear.

Recommendation. Separately label sources for sync latency / batch dry-run / per-call cost / retry-adjusted effective cost. Cost is not in LP-606's decision frame; it stays as reference material. Detail in [Appendix G](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.xw65wziu9mgy).  
6.10 A11 — Backfill timeframe  
Context. The Apr 27 Spec Kick-off note posed "Do we need to plan for any backfill timeframe with this feature?" without an answer recorded.

Options.

- No backfill (default assumption) — at launch, only cold-start users gradually receive coaching. Engineering Docs estimate cold-start ramp-down at \~21 days.  
- Day-1 backfill — single batch generation for all eligible users right before/after launch. Requires Option 1 (batch) infrastructure, conflicting with LP-606's Option 2 single-path assumption.  
- Targeted backfill — accelerate cold-start only for a specific segment (e.g., 6+ photos & low diversity). Possible with Option 2 \+ a one-off external batch call.

Recommendation. No backfill (keep default assumption). The 21-day cold-start ramp-down is short enough to gather post-launch data, and Day-1 backfill breaks the Option 2 single-path assumption. If post-launch Profile Home view rate is low, revisit Targeted backfill as a follow-up.

If the meeting decides differently, add a backfill path to the [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) trigger gate and add pre-fill logic to the [§5.6 B7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.g9cgep2lrbzv) cache.  
7\. Appendices  
A. API Contract Detail  
A.1 Reference endpoint  
POST /v1/photo-review. Single boundary for SOUP calling AURA. Used for both request-time and background generation paths under Option 2 On-demand Sync.  
A.2 P0 required request fields  
Same as [§5.2 B2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.ju3zuxfeh321).  
A.3 P1 optional request fields

| Field | Status | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| target\_gender | Optional | multi-gender supported, array |
| city | Optional | prompt context. Not an MVP blocker |
| job\_titles | Optional | array |
| employers | Optional | array |
| schools | Optional | array |
| languages | Optional | multi-language follow-up |
| anthem | Optional | personalization fuel |
| lifestyles | Optional | personalization fuel |
| basics | Optional | personalization fuel |
| relationship\_intent | Optional | future tone/personalization |
| photos\[\].smartphoto\_score | TBD | tie-breaker candidate. coverage issues |

A.4 Request field decisions

| Decision | Proposal |
| :---- | :---- |
| country\_code | Fixed 2-letter ISO code |
| target\_gender | Fixed array |
| job/company/school | Fixed array |
| numeric enum vs string | Even if SOUP sends numeric enum, AURA/ML layer maps to LLM-friendly string |
| photo path | bucket \+ s3\_key default. Do not accept both formats simultaneously |
| prompt/model metadata | Always include prompt\_version, prompt\_name, model\_name in response and log |

A.5 Response shape candidate (Figma 6-element \+ LLM skip branch)  
Figma displays information in the order bottom sheet (title/body) → "Review" button → Edit Photos screen (coach title/body \+ problematic photo display). The backend response returns these 6 elements together in one call; if AURA judges the user is already diverse/non-repetitive, it returns an empty coaching via the status="skip" branch ([§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915)).

A. status="success" — normal coaching response (combined model, [§3.2.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.6ip59ri0fi4n) Q1.2 recommendation)

```json
{
  "request_id": "71639584-1234-5678-9012-345678901234",
  "status": "success",
  "model_name": "gemini/gemini-3.1-pro-preview",
  "prompt_name": "photo-coaching-2026-03-17",
  "prompt_version": "v4",
  "bottom_sheet_title": "We have profile improvement tips",
  "bottom_sheet_body": "Adding a bit more variety to your photos can lead to more match opportunities",
  "coach_title": "Vary your photo angles more",
  "coach_body": "Your photos are mostly selfies. Adding a full-body shot or an outdoor photo gives users a more dimensional impression.",
  "per_photo_problems": [
    {"photo_id": "abc-123", "problem_description": "The strong filter makes face recognition difficult"},
    {"photo_id": "def-456", "problem_description": "Angle/style is similar to other photos, lacks variety"}
  ]
}
```

(If Q1.2 picks the split model, problematic\_photo\_ids: \["abc-123", "def-456"\] is added as a separate field.)

B. status="skip" — LLM judges "no coaching needed"

```json
{
  "request_id": "71639584-1234-5678-9012-345678901234",
  "status": "skip",
  "skip_reason": "already_diverse",
  "model_name": "gemini/gemini-3.1-pro-preview",
  "prompt_name": "photo-coaching-2026-03-17",
  "prompt_version": "v4"
}
```

When status="skip", the 6 element fields are empty or omitted. SOUP does not store in cache and records a coaching\_generation\_skipped event (skip\_reason=already\_diverse).

Open questions:

- The 6 element names above are candidates that map 1:1 to Figma. Naming stability is decided in [§6.1 A7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.c19rdsusi8hi).  
- problematic\_photo\_ids is just the photo\_id extracted from per\_photo\_problems. Whether to keep them split or combine is decided in [§3.2.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.6ip59ri0fi4n) Q1.2.  
- Additional LLM-derived element candidates (severity, cta\_label, recommended\_swap\_photo, overall\_score, repetitive\_clusters, rank\_in\_cluster) are discussed in [§3.2 A2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg).  
- skip\_reason enum starts with hypotheses like already\_diverse, low\_repetitiveness, insufficient\_input.  
- If localization is handled in the backend, the response shape changes to a localization-key form.

B. Option 2 Flow  
B.1 Base flow  
Day N — session in which coaching is generated:

1. The user opens the app.  
2. SOUP-side deterministic gate ([§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) Stage 1\) checks eligibility.  
3. If dismissed, profile\_version equals cached version, or last generation is the same calendar day as today, do not call.  
4. Otherwise SOUP calls AURA via POST /v1/photo-review.  
5. AURA receives profile/photo/context and runs a Gemini sync call.  
6. AURA-side LLM-derived gate ([§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) Stage 2): if LLM judges "already diverse / non-repetitive," returns status="skip" \+ skip\_reason; otherwise returns status="success" \+ 6 elements.  
7. SOUP stores the result in the profile\_version-keyed cache when status="success" (hard ceiling 30 days). On status="skip", no cache and a coaching\_generation\_skipped event is recorded.  
8. If the user reaches a persistent surface like Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper within the session, ready coaching appears there. The bottom sheet is not shown in this session.  
9. On timeout or failure, no coaching is shown in this session.

Day N+1 onward — next app open:

10. The user opens the app again.  
11. SOUP checks for cache hit (assuming profile\_version unchanged).  
12. If a coaching with cache ready, viewed=false, and dismissed\_at null exists, the bottom sheet appears as a nudge at app open.  
13. When the user taps the bottom sheet, they navigate to the Edit Photos screen and see coach\_title / coach\_body / per\_photo\_problems.  
14. On dismiss, eligibility is removed per [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm).

C. Ownership Model

| Component | Recommended ownership |
| :---- | :---- |
| Client | rendering, visible surfaces, ready-state UI, bottom sheet behavior |
| SOUP backend | eligibility, product state, profile snapshot, exposure history, day-boundary check, AURA invocation |
| AURA / MGAI | prompt/model/version management, prompt assembly, Gemini call, structured response generation, model/prompt metadata, inference logs |
| Storage / cache | product state on SOUP/product backend. inference-only cache may live on AURA but separated from product state |

D. Persistence Choices (reference)  
D.1 Strict ephemeral  
No storage. Conflicts with the [§3.1 A1+A3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) decision ("keep same coaching when photos do not change"), so not adopted.  
D.2 On-demand \+ profile\_version-keyed cache (adopted)  
Reuse the same cache entry indefinitely while the profile is unchanged. Satisfies both cost savings and user-experience consistency. Set only a hard ceiling (e.g., 30 days) for retention. "No same-day new generation" is handled by the day-boundary check in the [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) trigger gate, not cache.  
D.3 Hybrid later  
Precompute cache or batch path is follow-up. Out of LP-606 scope.  
E. Bottom sheet timing — risks and mitigations  
Per the [§3.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) decision, the bottom sheet is shown only at the next app open (Evan \+ Jaini agreement, 4/24\~25). The remaining risks and mitigations under this policy are summarized below.

| Risk | Mitigation |
| :---- | :---- |
| If the user does not visit Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper in the same session, no coaching is shown that session | The next-app-open bottom sheet pulls the user back. The first opportunity yields to surfaces; the second is guaranteed by the bottom sheet |
| Bottom sheet appears too often, causing user fatigue | Once dismissed, eligibility is removed per [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm). Cap is decided in [§3.2.4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.2cphljq6gksq) |
| User receives it abruptly without prior notice | Review introduction copy / onboarding. Add opt-out if needed |
| Cache is stale at bottom sheet exposure (profile changed in the meantime) | profile\_version-keyed cache auto-invalidates on change. After invalidation, new generation the next day |
| Coaching generated on Day N, user did not visit the surface, and Day N+1 app open shows the bottom sheet directly — risk of feeling like an ad | Use bottom sheet copy in a referential tone like "a tip prepared in your previous session". Image approach ([§3.2.4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.2cphljq6gksq)) aligns with this tone |

F. Reliability and Observability Detail  
F.1 Timeout  
p99 is around 30.5 seconds, so design around a 30-second budget. Late results after timeout flow into the [§5.6 B7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.g9cgep2lrbzv) cache and are used in the next surface/session. Timeout/failure are recorded as observability events.  
F.2 Retry

- SOUP does not re-call the same request.  
- Single in-AURA transient retry within a 30-second budget.  
- Retry count, backoff, and timeout budget explicit.

F.3 Idempotency / dedupe

- request\_id: tracing and idempotency  
- dedupe key: (user\_id, profile\_version or snapshot\_hash, prompt\_version, model\_name)  
- If the same dedupe key is in-flight, no new Gemini call is started. Retry keeps the same key.

F.4 MVP observability set  
See [Analytics Event Taxonomy Detail](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.mgcphs7lx54y).  
G. Cost and Latency Inputs  
G.1 Known numbers

| Metric | Value | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| sync p50 | \~17.5 s | Gemini Flash-Lite sync call |
| sync p95 | \~25 s | Gemini Flash-Lite sync call |
| sync p99 | \~30.5 s | Drives timeout budget |
| test region Option 2 upper bound | \~$66K/month | Varies with trigger rate assumption |
| global Option 2 upper bound | \~$325K/month | Global run rate. Separated from experiment cost |
| batch dry-run observed median | \~16.8 min | Gemini 2.5 batch dry-run. Option 1 reference |

G.2 Open issue  
The following must be labeled separately.

- Which model/config is sync latency measured on?  
- Which model/config is the batch dry-run on?  
- Which model/pricing/discount is per-call cost on?  
- What is the retry-included effective cost?

In the LP-606 decision frame, cost is not used as a decision item (reference material).  
Analytics Event Taxonomy Detail

| Category | Event | Emit owner | Meaning / measurement goal |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Generation lifecycle | coaching\_generation\_requested | SOUP | Just before AURA call after trigger gate passes |
| Generation lifecycle | coaching\_generation\_succeeded | AURA | Gemini call success, response returned |
| Generation lifecycle | coaching\_generation\_failed | AURA | Includes failure reason |
| Generation lifecycle | coaching\_generation\_skipped | SOUP | skip\_reason (same\_day\_already\_generated / no\_profile\_change / ineligible / dismissed) |
| Surface impression | coaching\_ready | SOUP | Result is exposable to the client |
| Surface impression | coaching\_ready\_but\_not\_viewed | Client | Not exposed by session end |
| Surface impression | coaching\_viewed | Client | Actually shown on a persistent surface |
| Surface impression | coaching\_clicked | Client | viewed → CTA or detail entry |
| Surface impression | coaching\_dismissed | Client | Dismissed on a persistent surface |
| Bottom sheet | bottom\_sheet\_impression | Client | Hook message shown |
| Bottom sheet | bottom\_sheet\_tap\_through | Client | Hook → detail entry |
| Bottom sheet | bottom\_sheet\_dismissed | Client | Bottom sheet itself dismissed |
| Bottom sheet | swipe\_drop\_off\_post\_impression | Client | Guardrail |
| Bottom sheet | session\_length\_post\_impression | Client | Guardrail |
| Profile change | profile\_edited\_after\_coaching | Client/SOUP | Change within N minutes after coaching exposure |
| Profile change | photo\_added\_after\_coaching | SOUP | Photo add event attribution |
| Profile change | photo\_removed\_after\_coaching | SOUP | Photo remove event attribution |
| Failure / skip | eligibility\_check\_result | SOUP | Gate pass/fail reason |
| Failure / skip | experiment\_arm\_assigned | Client/SOUP | Control vs treatment allocation |

Common dimensions (attached to every event): request\_id, user\_id, profile\_version, prompt\_version, model\_name, experiment\_arm, surface, session\_id.  
H. Option 1 related Out-of-scope items  
Not directly addressed in the LP-606 Option 2 kick-off.

| Topic | Reason for separation |
| :---- | :---- |
| How SOUP gathers an hourly batch eligible user list | Option 1 batch architecture only |
| How many users/photos are processed in the hourly batch | Option 1 capacity planning only |
| Source of 17-min batch turnaround | Source needs to be specified in Option 1 decision doc |
| Whether SOUP must build new eligible-user-list infra | Big impact on Option 1 LOE |

I.1 Trigger frequency / per-app-open call ✅  
"Joining the party late so sorry if I am missing context... What is the reasoning for triggering this on every app open? Won't we waste compute on users who don't change their photos or already received coaching?" — Evan Keys, 4/24 1:52 AM

"I have similar question in a comment below.. 'should this be each app open or each app open AND any changes to the input i.e. new upload, deletions or replacement of their photo.?' @[trideep.rath@gotinder.com](mailto:trideep.rath@gotinder.com) and I talked about the latter which I added to the product spec." — Jaini Shah, 4/24 2:07 AM

"should this be each app open or each app open and any changes to the input i.e. new upload, deletions or replacement of their photo.?" — Jaini Shah, 4/23 5:27 AM

Resolution: [§3.1 A1+A3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) (keep same coaching if profile unchanged, new coaching the next day if changed) · [§3.3 A4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.q4iaelimp80o) (skip target set) · [§3.4 A5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.upygd9ysc76a) (app open as single trigger).  
I.2 Same-session nudge vs next app open ✅  
"Why do we need to nudge the user in the same session we trigger coaching generation for option 2? I think users are nudged/disrupted enough mid swipe so adding another I think is a risk. It should be feasible to save state that is read on next app open giving an experience similar to option 1." — Evan Keys, 4/24 1:56 AM

"agree. I don't think we need to nudge them in the same session. The way i was thinking about the user experience is that once the coaching is ready, it shows up in the persistent surface areas (i.e. profile home, edit photos, photo cropper) and then at next app open is when the bottom sheet could show up. I believe this is similar to what growth opted for as well and also this approach makes sense with engagement team as well." — Jaini Shah, 4/25 3:49 AM

"if the user skips the nudge or skips viewing this coaching, would it be available to them the next app open? curious about session length per user and possibility of a user missing this (apart from disruptiveness causing them to miss this coaching moment). @[kevin.celustka@gotinder.com](mailto:kevin.celustka@gotinder.com) wdyt? cc: @[juniper.han@match.com](mailto:juniper.han@match.com) @[trideep.rath@gotinder.com](mailto:trideep.rath@gotinder.com)" — Jaini Shah, 4/23 4:35 AM

"Possible in theory, but it has to be orchestrated from backend. Basically some state saving logic has to be incorporated by backend. App open \--\> Is user eligible and has not seen feedback \--\> feedback service \--\> Feedback saved \--\> Bottom sheet displayed" — Trideep Rath, 4/23 6:12 AM

"can't it be surfaced and ready for them to access in the next session (if they are returning and no profile change)?" — Jaini Shah, 4/23 4:41 AM

"Yes \- Bottom sheet nudge cc: @[nancy.wu@gotinder.com](mailto:nancy.wu@gotinder.com)" — Jaini Shah, 4/23 5:26 AM

Resolution: [§2 Exec Summary conclusion 6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.k0j6n3y84wj8) · [§3.2 What we're deciding](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) (Day N: persistent surfaces, Day N+1: bottom sheet) · [Appendix B](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.koy3dw3emuv5) (Day N \+ Day N+1 flow) · [Appendix E](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.mvszifhvz0zr) (next-app-open policy risks/mitigations).

I.10 Cost tradeoff framing (long-term) 🟡  
"I still don't have a very concrete idea how to make the tradeoff decision. In my mind this is a bread an butter feature, so we are not necessarily trying to prove the value of the feature here. If we see from this lens would we have to refactor this to make it work from the cost perspective in future or should we make that decision from the get go. cc: @[ben.shin@gotinder.com](mailto:ben.shin@gotinder.com)" — Trideep Rath, 4/23 7:43 AM

"Also another thing to consider here is that the cost of this is not necessarily going to stay the same. The cost of apis are coming down, if we need to justify it from the cost perspective we could serve something inhouse." — Trideep Rath, 4/23 7:48 AM

"In general I think its ok to test a proof of concept before we worry about how to pay for it\! We might learn there is no cash upside to the treatment, but there are some users worth providing this feature to (users who are struggling or subscribers etc) More concerned with cost of experiment than monthly global run rate." — Kevin Celustka, 4/23 7:52 AM

Resolution: Cost is excluded from the LP-606 decision frame (see [§6.9 B13](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.x8lztd982ul1), [Appendix G.3 Decision framing](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.xw65wziu9mgy)). Long-term cost refactor potential and in-house serving are follow-up tracks (out of LP-606 scope). 🟡
