## 1\. 30-Minute Session Guide

The reading order of the doc is the meeting order.

| Order | Section | Time | Goal |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | [§2 Executive Summary](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.k0j6n3y84wj8) | 3 min | Agree on the recommendation paragraph and the decision-result paragraph. Yes/no on "the big-picture direction is correct" |
| 2 | [§3 Track A — Required Product Decisions](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.15m0x797spk8) | 12 min | Close A1+A3, A2, A4, A5, A6 in sequence |
| 3 | [§4 Hand-off Map](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.do682u62dlny) | 3 min | Confirm what Track A outputs feed into Track B |
| 4 | [§5 Track B — Required Engineering Decisions](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.v7w1qmlfbg0z) | 10 min | Close B1, B2/B3, B4, B5, B6, B7 in sequence |
| 5 | [§6 Optional / Follow-up](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.s7bybr323135) | Remainder | A7, A9, A10, A11 (backfill), B8–B13. If time runs short, set owner and due date and defer to async |

Every decision item uses the same box format.

**What we're deciding.** State the decision question in a plain paragraph that every stakeholder can understand at once.  
**Recommendation.** The recommended option and its rationale.  
**Risk if not decided.** What concrete work gets blocked if we defer.  
**Why this matters in this session.** (Secondary) Why we must close it here. Read only if the urgency is unclear from the three items above.  
**Question for the room.** One or two sharp questions to drop in the meeting.  
**Agreement (fill in during meeting).** Capture the agreed outcome on the spot.

## 2\. Executive Summary

Stakeholder discussion has already settled the serving direction as **Option 2 (On-demand Sync)**. The goal of this kick-off is not to finish the entire backend design but to enable SOUP backend and AURA/MGAI to run parallel implementation through next quarter. To do that, this session handles two things at once: (1) the items product must answer before engineering starts and (2) the items engineering must freeze in the contract once those answers land.

Recommendation paragraph (product view):

Photo Review **shows new coaching the next day when the user changes a photo, and keeps the prior coaching when nothing changes**. Coaching is generated at app open, but **within that session it appears only on persistent surfaces (Profile Home, Edit Photos, Photo Cropper)**. **The bottom sheet appears as a nudge on the next app open**, and tapping it opens the Edit Photos screen with the coach title/body and the repetitive-cluster-driven per-photo ℹ️ indicator. Dismissing it stops further coaching for the MVP starting point — engineering suggestion pending PM ratification (Jaini/Juniper); see [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm) and [§2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.k0j6n3y84wj8) Conclusion 7\.

Unpacked, this becomes the following 8 conclusions.

1. The SOUP → AURA contract freezes as a single endpoint, POST /v1/photo-review. We do not build auxiliary endpoints like status/result/cancel.  
     
2. The trigger entry point is **app open only**. **Engineering suggestion (pending PM ratification by Jaini/Juniper)**: at most one AURA call per user per day, with a 1-calendar-day cool-down between insights (Evan, 4/24 inline comment surfaced the once-per-day question). SOUP handles that cooldown internally and calls AURA only when the user is eligible; `last_generated_at` is only a possible SOUP-internal reference field, not an AURA contract field. Profile Home / Edit Photos are result-display surfaces, not triggers.  
     
   **Update on 4/27**: Yes, the trigger is app-open only.  
     
- **Important note**: The bottom sheet, however, will be triggered on the next app open so the user gets the alert when they enter the app, not mid-swipe.  
    
  For post D0,  
    
- **Engineering suggestion (pending PM ratification by Jaini/Juniper)**: Users who have dismissed the previous coaching are **not** eligible for any further coaching (X \= full opt-out for MVP, no auto-resume on photo change). 4/28 Spec Kick-off explicitly logged dismiss policy as an open question (Jaini L391; Ryan punted complex opt-out to post-MVP, L439); MVP retains the original engineering-doc stance.  
    
- Users who change a photo (and have not dismissed) get new coaching after a cool-down between insights. **Engineering suggestion (pending PM ratification by Jaini/Juniper)**: 1 calendar day. Any lifetime max-insights cap belongs with the SOUP eligibility / frequency gate in [§3.3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.q4iaelimp80o), not the bottom-sheet image UX section.  
    
3. **Same coaching when photos do not change; new coaching the next day when they do.** SOUP owns product state and cached coaching. Field names such as `photo_review_opt_in`, `last_generated_at`, and the photo-change signal / `profile_version` placeholder are SOUP-internal references only; AURA does not receive or decide them.  
     
4. AURA owns the inference boundary as well as prompt/model versioning. That is, prompt/model versioning, prompt assembly, the Gemini call, structured response, prompt/model metadata, and the inference log are all AURA's responsibility.  
     
5. Persistence is a photo-change-signal-keyed cache on the SOUP side. The same cache entry keeps getting reused as long as the photo set is unchanged. We set a hard ceiling (e.g., 30 days) for retention. Strict ephemeral is not adopted.  
     
6. **The bottom sheet appears only on the next app open, not in the same session** (Evan \+ Jaini agreement, 2026-04-24\~25). In the same session, coaching is shown only on persistent surfaces (Profile Home, Edit Photos, Photo Cropper); the bottom sheet appears as a nudge at the next app open. The backend response returns 5 elements together in a single call — bottom\_sheet\_title / bottom\_sheet\_body, coach\_title / coach\_body, and `repetitive_clusters` (which drives the per-photo ℹ️ indicator; see [§3.2.1](#3.2.1-backend-response-—-visible-elements-mapping) for the post-4/28 simplification). The elements themselves are exactly as in Figma; only the exposure timing of the bottom sheet shifts to the next session.  
     
7. Dismiss is not a short-term block but **permanent removal from eligibility** (a re-invitation campaign is a separate follow-up). The 4/28 Spec Kick-off surfaced two competing reads (per-insight dismiss vs full feature opt-out) and Jaini explicitly logged it as an open question rather than a decision (transcript line 391; Ryan punted complex opt-out logic to post-MVP, line 439). **Engineering suggestion (pending PM ratification by Jaini/Juniper)**: retain the original engineering doc stance — X \= full opt-out for MVP, no auto-resume on profile photo change. Simplest behavior; defer per-insight dismiss to post-MVP.  
     
8. Retry is not a SOUP re-call but a single in-AURA transient retry within a 30-second budget. The dedupe key is (user\_id, SOUP-internal photo-change signal, prompt\_version, model\_name); prompt/model versioning is a separate cache dimension, not an input to the photo-change signal.

**Deliberate delta from Engineering Docs** (this is the v2 follow-up). The original [Photo Review MVP Engineering Docs](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U) defined Option 2 as *"Ephemeral. No stored inferences"*, and the Coaching Store was specified as Option 1 only (MGAI-owned). This doc adds a SOUP-side cache keyed by the user and SOUP's internal photo-change signal, with prompt/model versions as separate cache dimensions. This preserves the same coaching for users whose photos have not changed and lets the result appear in the next session. Also, per the Apr 22 Status Update doc decision, *"Custom ML-model based approach will not be included in MVP Photo Review"* — i.e., the self-hosted GPU step is dropped from MVP and AURA calls Gemini directly.

### 2.1 Decision Map (this session's scope)

| Class | ID | Name | Close in this session | Where | Detail |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Required (Product) | A1+A3 | When users see new coaching (next day if photos change, same coaching if not) | Yes | [§3.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) | confirm |
| Required (Product) | A2 | Coaching surface exposure model \+ LLM output definition (4 sub-decisions) | Yes | [§3.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) | clarify \+ decide |
| Required (Product) | A4 | Skip rules | Yes | [§3.3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.q4iaelimp80o) | confirm |
| Required (Product) | A5 | Trigger surface scope | Yes | [§3.4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.upygd9ysc76a) | confirm |
| Required (Product) | A6 | Dismissed policy | Yes | [§3.5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm) | confirm |
| Required (Engineering) | B1 | API endpoint | Yes | [§5.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.utdhzivpsb7i) | freeze |
| Required (Engineering) | B2 \+ B3 | request hydration boundary \+ photo path | Yes | [§5.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.ju3zuxfeh321) | freeze |
| Required (Engineering) | B4 | Trigger gate owner | Yes | [§5.3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) | freeze |
| Reference (Engineering) | B5 | SOUP-owned product-state reference | No | [§5.4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.rk2a2g52g598) | reference only |

## 3\. Track A — Required Product Decisions

Audience: PM / Photo Review PM / Growth-Engagement / Design.

These 5 decisions must close before [§5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.v7w1qmlfbg0z) (Engineering). If they remain open, SOUP/MGAI have to assume the contract and storage shape, and the cost of changing them post-launch grows.

### 3.1 A1+A3 — When do users see new coaching

**Severity**: P0

**What we're deciding.** When a user who has received Photo Review changes a **photo**, **when** should new coaching appear (same day / next day), and when a user opens the app the next day without changing any photo, **which coaching** should they see (yesterday's coaching / a freshly generated one). Once these two product questions are answered, the backend's storage shape and call frequency follow automatically. As a side decision, we also need to choose **what to show** during the gap between a photo change and the next-day new coaching (previous coaching as-is / a "we'll let you know soon" notice / empty state).

**Recommendation.**

- **Q1 \= next day.** Do not show new coaching the same day. This is consistent with PM view. Multiple new coachings on the same day fatigue the user and amplify the "change a photo → change another photo" pressure.  
- **Q2 \= keep the same coaching.** If the profile photo has not changed, there is no reason for the coaching content to differ. Generating fresh coaching every time creates inconsistency where the same user sees different coachings, and burns cost for no value.

The two answers combine into a one-line behavior:

**New coaching the next day when the user's photos change; otherwise keep the prior coaching.**

**User-perspective scenario.**

- Monday morning: receives first coaching.  
- Monday afternoon: adds a photo. → No new coaching same day (prior Monday coaching kept, or empty state, per Q3).  
- Tuesday morning: new coaching (reflecting the changed photos).  
- Wednesday morning: no photo change. → Sees Tuesday's coaching as-is.  
- Thursday onward: no photo change. → Continues to see Tuesday's coaching.

**Confirmed by source.** Engineering Docs [§3.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) ([Photo Review MVP Engineering Docs](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U)) originally cited a 5-field trigger set (photo / bio / prompt / interest / descriptor). **Narrowed for MVP (4/28, post-meeting reconciliation): photos-only** — see [§5.5 B6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.r1xgqe953h07) for rationale (Evan, 4/24 inline comment: non-photo edits would burn AURA cost without lift for photo coaching).

**Exact definition of photo change (MVP):**

- photo add  
- photo delete  
- photo replace

Photo reorder, bio/prompt/interest/descriptor edits, and core fields (age/gender/country/relationship intent) are not in the MVP trigger set. This set must map 1:1 to the [§5.5 B6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.r1xgqe953h07) photo-change signal trigger.

**Risk if not decided.**

- "Same-day new coaching" raises both user burden and cost.  
- "Generate fresh coaching daily even without photo change" makes the same user see different coachings, eroding product trust.  
- If the two answers stay ambiguous, backend cannot lock storage shape or call frequency.

**Why this matters in this session.** If "when does the user receive new coaching" is not frozen on the product side, backend has to proceed on assumed storage / call frequency / cache invalidation rules. Once launched, the meaning of storage is hard to change, so deciding here is the cheapest path.

**Question for the room (product level only).**

1. **Q1**: For a user who changes a photo the same day, is it better to surface new coaching the same day, or the next day?  
   1. Next day  
2. **Q2**: For a user whose photos have not changed, how many days is it acceptable to keep showing the same coaching? (forever / refresh after some period / other)  
   1. Forever until dismissal or feature removal  
2. **Q3**: Right after a photo change and before the next-day new coaching arrives, what do we show? Previous coaching? "New coaching coming soon" notice? Empty state?  
   1. Some sort of celebratory & new coaching coming soon message \-\> will align with design for this screen

**Agreement (fill in during meeting).**

- Q1 (same day / next day): Next day  
- Q2 (keep / refresh after N days): Keep  
- Q3 (previous coaching / notice / empty state): Notice  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

**Engineering note (PM may skip).** If the answers settle on next day \+ keep same coaching, SOUP implements (a) an internal one-calendar-day cooldown and (b) a photo-change-signal-keyed cache. A 30-day hard ceiling is enough from a retention standpoint. See [§5.6 B7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.g9cgep2lrbzv) for implementation detail.

### 3.2 A2 — Coaching surface exposure model \+ LLM output definition

**Severity**: P0 (response schema and surface exposure policy affect client/SOUP/AURA)

**What we're deciding.** The latest Figma already includes the coach information shown on the bottom sheet and the Edit Photos screen. However, per Evan/Jaini's 2026-04-24\~25 agreement, **the bottom sheet appears only at the next app open, not in the same session** — within the same session, coaching appears only on persistent surfaces (Profile Home, Edit Photos, Photo Cropper). On top of that, this slot closes 4 operational decisions — (i) which visible elements the backend response returns in a single call and in what shape, (ii) how to present a repetitive photo cluster to the user, (iii) whether AURA should return an LLM-derived skip decision, and (iv) which visual treatment the bottom sheet uses. Max-insights / frequency caps belong to [§3.3 A4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.q4iaelimp80o), not bottom-sheet UX.

**Surface exposure model in one line** (Evan \+ Jaini agreement, 2026-04-24\~25):

- **Day N (the session in which coaching is generated)**: shown only on persistent surfaces (Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper). Do not interrupt while the user is swiping.  
- **Day N+1 onward (next app open)**: bottom sheet appears as a nudge. Tapping it opens the Edit Photos screen.  
- **Reference quotes**: Evan (4/24): *"Why do we need to nudge the user in the same session we trigger coaching generation for option 2? ... It should be feasible to save state that is read on next app open giving an experience similar to option 1."* / Jaini (4/25): *"once the coaching is ready, it shows up in the persistent surface areas (i.e. profile home, edit photos, photo cropper) and then at next app open is when the bottom sheet could show up."*

This decision splits into 4 topics. The meeting follows the same order.

| Sub-section | Topic | Decision form |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| [3.2.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.6ip59ri0fi4n) | Backend 5-element mapping (post-4/28 simplification) | freeze |
| [3.2.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.40bkz0jhc7gi) | Repetitive photo handling model | choose 1 of 4 |
| [3.2.3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.m5tvplya6ieb) | AURA-derived skip decision | confirm |
| [3.2.4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.2cphljq6gksq) | Bottom sheet visual treatment by coaching scenario | discuss \+ decide |

The operational rules sit on top of the 4 sub-section decisions.

- **Day N (the session in which coaching is generated)**: do not show the bottom sheet. If the user enters Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper, coaching appears there. If the user does not enter those surfaces, no coaching appears in that session.  
- **Day N+1 onward (next app open)**: for users whose cache has a ready coaching they have not yet viewed, the bottom sheet appears as a nudge at app open. Engineering suggestion (pending PM ratification): once dismissed, eligibility is removed per [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm).  
- **After a user takes a photo action in-session**: remove the current coaching/ℹ️ state from that session and show the default or success state; do **not** call AURA immediately. The next eligible app open is the refresh point. If the user changed the photo set and the cooldown allows it, SOUP calls AURA then; otherwise the user stays on the default / no-current-insight state.  
- Bottom sheet metrics map to the bottom\_sheet\_\* category in [§6.3 A10](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.j607oxyxzrxc).

**Engineering note (PM may skip).** Verifying that AURA can stably produce all response elements in one call within prompt/token limits is covered by the SOUP → AURA API contract and reliability follow-ups. Client-facing ready/read mechanics are SOUP / Client surface work, not an AURA contract decision.

#### 3.2.1 Backend response — visible elements mapping

**What we're deciding.** Figma shows the user 4 visible copy elements (bottom sheet title/body, and coach title/body on the Edit Photos screen after click-through) plus a per-photo **ℹ️ "i" indicator** rendered on members of a repetitive cluster. We decide **which field names and which shape** the backend uses to return these elements in a single call.

**Scope simplification (4/28 — Brandon, surfacing product call from spec kick-off):** the per-photo ℹ️ indicator is driven **entirely by the repetitive-cluster signal** ([§3.2.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.40bkz0jhc7gi)). MVP does **not** need a separate `per_photo_problems` array of detailed per-photo descriptions — every flagged photo in MVP carries the same conceptual reason ("this photo is repetitive with another in your set"), so a single cluster-level signal is enough to drive both the ℹ️ rendering and the (post-MVP) enlarged-view caption. Per-photo `problem_description` is dropped from the contract; it can be added later if and when non-repetitive per-photo issues need their own visual treatment.

**Figma flow and the visible elements (MVP).**

```
[App open]
   └─ ready state → bottom sheet appears
       ├─ ① bottom_sheet_title          (one-line title)
       └─ ② bottom_sheet_body            (benefit copy, "why look")
           ├─ "Review" tap →
           └─ Edit Photos screen
               ├─ ③ coach_title          (one-line problem title)
               ├─ ④ coach_body            (suggested action body)
               └─ ⑤ repetitive_clusters  (drives the per-photo ℹ️ "i" indicator)
```

These 5 elements are outputs of the same generation, so the AURA response **returns them together in one call**.

| Element | Candidate field name | Shape | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| ① bottom sheet title | bottom\_sheet\_title | string | one-line attention copy |
| ② bottom sheet body | bottom\_sheet\_body | string | benefit copy |
| ③ coach title | coach\_title | string | problem title on Edit Photos screen |
| ④ coach body | coach\_body | string | suggested action detail |
| ⑤ repetitive clusters | repetitive\_clusters | array of `{cluster_id, kept_photo_id, flagged_photo_ids[], cluster_label}` | drives ℹ️ rendering. Array order \= severity (worst-performing cluster first). Empty array \= no per-photo ℹ️ shown |

**Copy formatting.** All title/body copy fields above (`bottom_sheet_title`, `bottom_sheet_body`, `coach_title`, `coach_body`, plus `cluster_label`) are returned as **markdown-formatted strings**; the LLM emits inline `**bold**` to highlight key tokens (e.g., "hiking", "concert"), and the client renders bold spans as-is. Side-by-side effort estimation for client-side markdown rendering is an engineering follow-up (Trideep/Evan, 4/28 inline meeting discussion).

**Recommendation.**

- Freeze the 5 elements above (1:1 with Figma \+ cluster signal).  
- Drop `per_photo_problems` from the MVP contract. The cluster signal alone drives ℹ️ rendering, and `coach_title` / `coach_body` carries any narrative the user needs.  
- `repetitive_clusters` is an empty array when no repetitive cluster exists — the user still sees `coach_title` / `coach_body` if there's general advice, just no ℹ️ flags.  
- **Cluster ordering \= severity** (4/28 — Brandon): AURA returns clusters in the order the client should surface them, with the worst-performing cluster at index 0\. This is how the client identifies "the most bad cluster" without a separate severity field. The "one-cluster-at-a-time" rendering rule from [§3.2.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.40bkz0jhc7gi) means the client effectively reads `repetitive_clusters[0]` until it's resolved, then moves to `repetitive_clusters[1]` on the next refresh.  
- `cluster_label` is a short LLM-generated string (e.g., "repetitive mirror selfies", "repeated gym shots") used for the enlarged-photo caption and any future per-cluster annotation. One label per cluster (not per photo), since all photos in a cluster share the same conceptual reason.

**Sample (MVP shape).**

```json
"repetitive_clusters": [
  {
    "cluster_id": "c1",
    "kept_photo_id": "abc-123",
    "flagged_photo_ids": ["def-456", "ghi-789"],
    "cluster_label": "repetitive mirror selfies"
  }
]
```

**Risk if not decided.**

- If Figma elements and backend fields don't map 1:1, client mapping wobbles right before launch.  
- If `repetitive_clusters` shape is left ambiguous, AURA can't lock prompt output schema.

**Question for the room.**

- Q1.1: Do the 5 elements above match Figma's information structure (post-simplification)?  
- Q1.2: ~~Split ⑤+⑥, or combine?~~ Resolved by dropping per-photo descriptions entirely; only `repetitive_clusters` remains.

**Agreement.**

- Freeze 5-element mapping (Yes / change): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Drop `per_photo_problems` for MVP (Yes / keep): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

#### 3.2.2 Repetitive photo handling model

**What we're deciding.** When a user's profile contains a repetitive cluster of similar photos, how do we present it to the user? Mark every photo in the cluster equally, focus on one cluster at a time, or highlight only the worst photo in the cluster — the model we pick determines whether the backend has to produce separate cluster grouping or ranking information.

Four models are possible: prior behavior, current Figma, Nancy's proposal (2026-04-08 Slack), and a worst-highlight variant.

| Model | Behavior | Required LLM output |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| (Prior) Best-keep | Don't mark the best photo in the cluster; mark the rest as "duplicate" | (legacy: per-photo flag) — superseded by `repetitive_clusters` post-4/28 |
| (Current Figma) Mark-all | Mark all repetitive photos in the cluster at the same depth | (legacy: per-photo flag) — superseded by `repetitive_clusters` post-4/28 |
| (Nancy proposal) **One-cluster-at-a-time** | Show only one cluster at a time; once resolved, surface the next cluster on the next visit | cluster grouping info needed (repetitive\_clusters or cluster\_id) |
| Worst-highlight | Strongly highlight the worst photo in a cluster; soft-mark the rest | repetitive\_clusters or per-photo rank\_in\_cluster |

**Nancy quote** (Photo Review Slack, 2026-04-08): *"we could only show 1 repetitive issue at a time ... the rationale is bc the copy on the profile home module is so tied to the edit profile one, that it feels like we'd have to keep the user focused on one photo issue at a time."*

**MVP element shape (post 4/28 simplification — see also [§3.2.1](#3.2.1-backend-response-—-visible-elements-mapping)):**

```json
"repetitive_clusters": [
  {
    "cluster_id": "c1",
    "kept_photo_id": "abc-123",
    "flagged_photo_ids": ["def-456", "ghi-789"],
    "cluster_label": "repetitive mirror selfies"
  }
]
```

- Array order \= severity (worst-performing cluster first). Client surfaces `repetitive_clusters[0]` until resolved, then moves to `[1]` on the next refresh.  
- `kept_photo_id` is the highest-RSR photo in the cluster — it is **not** flagged with ℹ️.  
- `flagged_photo_ids` are the lower-RSR cluster members that get the ℹ️ indicator.  
- `cluster_label` is a short LLM-generated string for the enlarged-photo caption.

**Recommendation.**

- Handling model is **Best-keep \+ One-cluster-at-a-time** (confirmed in 4/28 Spec Kick-off — Jaini/Juniper/Trideep). Within a cluster, the highest-RSR photo is **kept unmarked**; the lower-RSR photos in the same cluster are flagged with the ℹ️ indicator. When a user has multiple repetitive clusters, surface only one cluster at a time and reveal the next on the following visit.  
- Cluster information shape: **single `repetitive_clusters` top-level array** (post-4/28 simplification — see [§3.2.1](#3.2.1-backend-response-—-visible-elements-mapping)). The earlier "inline cluster\_id \+ rank\_in\_cluster inside per\_photo\_problems" shape is dropped along with `per_photo_problems` itself.  
- **Figma update pending** — current Figma marks all photos in a cluster equally; Nancy to update so the highest-RSR photo in a cluster is unmarked (4/28 action).

**Scope clarification (4/28 product decision, surfaced by Brandon — engineering captures it here for the contract):**

1. **The per-photo Info indicator (ℹ️ "i" icon in Figma) is shown *only* on members of a repetitive cluster.** Non-repetitive issues (e.g., heavy filter, similar angle, low light) are surfaced through `coach_title` / `coach_body` text only — they do **not** trigger per-photo flags or Info indicators.  
2. **Replacement recommendations may still appear in coaching copy, but they do not create per-photo ℹ️ markers.** If the recommendation is tied to a repetitive cluster, the lower-RSR members of that cluster are flagged. If the recommendation is not tied to a repetitive cluster, it stays in `coach_title` / `coach_body` / action copy only.  
3. **The per-photo Info indicator is therefore not a general "replace this photo" marker.** It is only the rendering affordance for photos in `repetitive_clusters[].flagged_photo_ids`.

This makes `repetitive_clusters[]` the single source of truth for ℹ️ rendering. It is empty when the user has no repetitive cluster. This also removes the need for a separate `recommended_swap_photo` response field in MVP: replacement guidance can live in general coaching copy, while per-photo markers are derived only from the surfaced repetitive cluster.

**Question for the room.**

- Q2.1: Of the 4 models, which matches product intent? (Recommendation: One-cluster-at-a-time)  
- Q2.2: ~~Cluster info as separate field vs inline in per\_photo\_problems?~~ Resolved by dropping `per_photo_problems` and using a top-level `repetitive_clusters` array (post-4/28 simplification).

**Agreement.**

- Handling model (Best-keep / Mark-all / **One-cluster-at-a-time** / Worst-highlight): One-cluster-at-a-time, with the highest-RSR photo unmarked  
- Cluster info shape: **top-level `repetitive_clusters` array** (single source of truth for ℹ️ rendering)  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

#### 3.2.3 AURA-derived skip decision

This section is intentionally narrow. Visible rendering data, including `repetitive_clusters[]` and the ℹ️ marker rule, is covered in [§3.2.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.6ip59ri0fi4n) and [§3.2.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.40bkz0jhc7gi). The only non-visible LLM-derived control signal AURA returns in MVP is whether coaching should be skipped because the profile is already sufficiently diverse / non-repetitive.

| Topic | Response element | Derivable only by LLM | Decision impact |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **AURA skip decision** | status (success/skip) \+ skip\_reason | Yes | Direct link to the two-stage gate in [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915). SOUP stores coaching only when status=success; status=skip records a skipped-generation event and does not create a coaching cache entry. |

**Recommendation.**

- **Adopt status (success/skip) \+ skip\_reason** — required to make the [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) Stage 2 LLM gate work. Initial skip reasons: `already_diverse`, `low_repetitiveness`, `insufficient_input`.  
- Do **not** add separate MVP fields for severity, recommended\_swap\_photo, overall\_score, cta\_label, or locale. These are either visible-rendering/product-copy concerns already handled elsewhere, or follow-up metadata that does not change the MVP client contract.

**Question for the room.**

- Q3.1: Do we adopt the behavior where AURA's LLM judges "this user is already diverse / non-repetitive" and returns status="skip"? (Recommendation: Yes)  
- Q3.2: Is status="skip" \+ skip\_reason the only non-visible LLM-derived control signal AURA returns in MVP? (Recommendation: Yes)

**Agreement.**

- Adopt LLM-derived skip signal (Yes / No): YES  
- Other non-visible LLM-derived control signals to include (none / \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_): None in MVP  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

#### 3.2.4 Bottom sheet UX (Spec Kick-off new)

**What we're deciding.** Bottom sheet exposure timing was decided in [§3.2 What we're deciding](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) as next app open. This sub-section is not about adding a new AURA signal. It only clarifies the bottom sheet's **visual treatment**: static/design-owned asset vs user-photo visual, and if user photos are used, whether the selection can be derived from existing response data.

We group the UX items posted in today's Spec Kick-off [Notes](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1VxtA1qjkyZshECqtrLOL7NDe5G8CJiV6Mltmm6HHurw).

**(a) Visual treatment by coaching scenario** (Spec Kick-off Notes list this discussion topic under Nancy Wu):

- Option 1 — shared visual: one visual works for both "add more photos" and "replace repetitive photos" coaching.  
- Option 2 — scenario-specific visual: those two coaching scenarios use different visuals because the user intent is different.

This is **not** deciding how many buttons/actions the bottom sheet can have. The bottom sheet may still have multiple actions if Product/Design wants them. This decision only concerns the visual shown with the bottom sheet.

**(b) If the visual uses user photos, which photos are shown?** The latest Figma fans out 3 photos like a card-game hand. If this is a static/design-owned asset, no backend decision is needed. If it uses user photos, selection must come from existing data (`repetitive_clusters[]`, client photo inventory, or client-side ranking), not a new AURA field.

| Candidate | Meaning | Contract impact |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Static/design-owned asset | Visual is bundled with the client or design system | No AURA/SOUP response change |
| User's own repetitive/problematic photos | Show the user the photos connected to the Replace coaching | Use `repetitive_clusters[].flagged_photo_ids`; no new AURA field |
| User's own best photos | Show a positive example from the user's profile | Needs an existing client ranking signal; otherwise follow-up |
| User-photo fan-out (current Figma) | Show several user photos as a neutral preview | Must specify whether photos come from `repetitive_clusters[]` or client-side ranking |
| Hybrid (Add=static, Replace=user photos) | Add has no specific problematic photo; Replace can point at repetitive photos | Works if Replace uses `repetitive_clusters[]` |

**Recommendation.**

- **Visual treatment \= scenario-specific.** "Add more photos" and "replace repetitive photos" have different user intent, so they should not be forced into one generic visual if design has bandwidth.  
- **Contract-safe MVP choice \= Hybrid (Add=static/design-owned asset, Replace=user photos from `repetitive_clusters[].flagged_photo_ids`).** Add targets users without enough photos to display, so a static asset is natural. Replace can use the repetitive photos already returned for the ℹ️ markers. No separate bottom-sheet image field is added to the AURA response.  
- The bottom sheet is an **entry point for each ready insight**, not a one-time feature introduction. If PM adopts a max-insights cap / cooldown, that rate-limits the entry point. The same insight should not be shown on every app open after it has already been dismissed/viewed.

**Non-contract UI follow-ups from the 4/28 walkthrough.**

- Feedback sheet on dismiss: Client/Product follow-up. Feedback options are placeholder in Figma; if collected, the expected implementation is client-side analytics similar to Photo Touchup, not a new AURA response field.  
- Photo tips sheet: Design/Client follow-up to check reuse of the existing Growth photo tips surface. No AURA/SOUP contract change.  
- Incendio vs native nudge, app-open priority, and conflicts with other app-open bottom sheets: Client/Growth/Incendio follow-up. The AURA contract only returns the coaching payload; it does not decide delivery framework or priority.  
- "Prompt" → "Caption" rename and photo cropper UI cleanup: Profile Home / Design follow-up, not Photo Review AURA contract. Nancy to annotate Figma for UI-only changes.

**Question for the room.**

- Q4.1: Should "add more photos" and "replace repetitive photos" share one generic visual, or use scenario-specific visuals? (Recommendation: scenario-specific)  
- Q4.2: For MVP, should Add use a static/design-owned asset and Replace use photos from `repetitive_clusters[].flagged_photo_ids`? (Recommendation: Yes)  
- Q4.3: If design wants a generic user-photo fan-out instead, what existing signal selects those photos? (`repetitive_clusters[]`, client ranking, or follow-up)  
- Q4.4: Should bottom sheet exposure be one-time per feature, or one-time per ready insight? (4/28 direction: one-time per ready insight, rate-limited by cap/cooldown)

**Agreement.**

- Visual treatment (shared / scenario-specific): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- MVP visual source (static / repetitive photos / hybrid): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- User-photo selection source, if any: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

### 3.3 A4 — Which users do we not show coaching to

**Severity**: P0

**What we're deciding.** The reason "Option 2 \= coaching on every app open unconditionally" does not apply is precisely this skip rule. If the rule isn't clear, the same user gets repeated coaching, fatigue piles up, cost balloons, and we end up with an incident post-launch. We need to lock who is excluded and where the exclusion gets evaluated.

**Recommendation.**

- **Why now.** This is Stage 1 input into [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915). If product does not freeze the skip set, SOUP's gate code can't be written and AURA can't decide what to put behind status="skip".

**Recommendation (skip targets).**

The following users get no new coaching. The judgement happens in two places — conditions decidable from input data alone are owned by **SOUP**, and conditions that need to look at the photos themselves go to **AURA (LLM)** (see [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915)).

- (SOUP) **User locale is non-English** (MVP is English-only — bucketed by language, not Geo. Even within an English-eligible Geo, non-English users are excluded from the experiment entirely. Evan \+ Juniper, 4/28).  
- (SOUP) User received coaching recently and photos have not changed since (per [§3.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) Q2, keep the same coaching)  
- (SOUP) User changed photos the same day (per [§3.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) Q1, new coaching the next day)  
- (SOUP) User is policy-ineligible due to experiment, region, privacy, age, etc.  
- (SOUP) User is in an active Profile Restrictions experiment geo/cohort/assignment, once finalized by SOUPD-129, because Photo Review should not overlap with Profile Restrictions treatment. Do **not** use photo count \< 4 by itself as a Photo Review skip condition; in Profile Restrictions, \< 4 photos only matters as part of an AND eligibility rule with missing bio/prompt and other experiment constraints.  
- (SOUP) User has dismissed per [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm)  
- (SOUP) User has reached the PM-ratified lifetime max-insights cap, if adopted. Engineering suggestion (pending PM ratification by Jaini/Juniper): 3 lifetime insights per user as an MVP starting point; PM may also choose no cap.  
- **(AURA / LLM)** User whose photos are sufficiently diverse and non-repetitive that LLM judges no coaching is needed — the Hybrid (high diversity / low repetitiveness) definition already exists on the product side, so we put the criteria in the prompt and the LLM evaluates.

**Eligibility segments specified in the Confluence WIP spec** ([WIP Photo Review & Feedback](https://gotinder.atlassian.net/wiki/spaces/SOUP/pages/1898905601), updated 2026-04-27):

| Segment | Audience | MVP coaching |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Segment 1 | 6+ photos & **low/medium diversity** | Yes |
| Segment 2 | \< 6 photos (diversity irrelevant) | Yes |
| Skip (LLM judgment) | 6+ photos & **high diversity** | No (LLM returns status="skip") |
| Exclude (SOUP experiment overlap) | active Profile Restrictions experiment geo/cohort/assignment | No (avoid overlapping experiments) |

**Risk if not decided.**

- The same user unintentionally receives repeated coaching, accumulating fatigue.  
- Even with post-launch data, product cannot consistently explain "why this user got coaching."

**Why this matters in this session.** SOUP must implement the deterministic gate from this set. If the set isn't frozen, SOUP can't start mock or integration. AURA also can't define what status="skip" covers without Stage 1 settled.

**Question for the room (product level only).**

1. Do we agree to use the SOUP/AURA skip criteria above as the baseline as-is? Yes  
2. Should Profile Restrictions overlap be excluded by finalized geo, active experiment assignment/cohort, or both? \-\> TBD,, but the latest thinking is we’ll exclude Photo Restrictions geo will be excluded from Photo Review experiment   
3. Do we agree that low photo count alone is **not** a Photo Review skip condition, unless the user also falls into an active Profile Restrictions overlap exclusion? \-\> YES  
4. For product consistency, should users who opted out of other nudges/features be auto-skipped here? \-\> NO

**Agreement (fill in during meeting).**

- Freeze SOUP/AURA skip criteria (Yes / change): YES  
- Profile Restrictions overlap rule (geo / cohort / assignment): TBD  
- Low-photo-count handling (not skipped by count alone / change): YES  
- Other-nudge opt-out user handling: NO  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

### 3.4 A5 — When do we generate coaching, and where does it appear

**Severity**: P0 (mostly confirm — PM agreement already exists)

**What we're deciding.** Among PMs, the agreement "generate at app open for every eligible user" already exists. We need to verify it once more in this slot. Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper are surfaces that **display** an already-generated result, not generation points. We also confirm whether deep-link entries (notification → app entry) follow the same model.

**Recommendation.**

- New coaching is generated only at app open.  
- Profile Home, Edit Photos, Photo Cropper entries serve only as result display surfaces.  
- Even if the same user opens the app multiple times the same day, no further new coaching is generated per [§3.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db).

**Risk if not decided.**

- If multiple entry points generate, the same user creates several coachings in a short time, raising user burden and cost.  
- If PM agreement is not verified, post-launch we get questions like "why doesn't X screen produce a fresh one?"

**Why this matters in this session.** "Verify PM agreement" sounds light but it locks SOUP's call model and cost estimate baseline. If we leave it open, both shake.

**Question for the room (product level only).**

1. Do all PMs agree on "new coaching only at app open; other screens are display surfaces"? \-\> YES  
2. What product signal would make us add Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper entry as a new coaching trigger later? (e.g., revisit if app-open conversion is low) \-\> REVISIT POST MVP   
3. Do deep-link cases (notification → app entry) get treated the same as a regular app open?-\> **YES but can you confirm here [Ryan Burns](mailto:ryan.burns@gotinder.com)**

**Agreement (fill in during meeting).**

- App open is the only new coaching trigger (Yes / add other screens): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Conditions for revisiting additional surface triggers: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Deep link handling (same / split): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

### 3.5 A6 — What happens after a user dismisses

**Severity**: P0

**What we're deciding.** What is the product meaning of the user action "dismiss"? Specifically, **after a user dismisses Photo Review's coaching, do they ever see it again? If so, under what conditions?** Without an answer, users react negatively ("why again?") and backend has no idea whether to keep generating for them.

**PM-side question (product level).**

If a user dismisses Photo Review coaching, will they **see coaching again** afterward? If yes, under what conditions?

**Recommendation (engineering suggestion — pending PM ratification by Jaini/Juniper).**

The 4/28 Spec Kick-off surfaced two competing reads (per-insight dismiss vs full feature opt-out) and Jaini explicitly logged this as an open question rather than a decision (transcript L391); Ryan punted complex opt-out logic to post-MVP (L439). MVP retains the original engineering-doc stance:

- Treat dismiss as a strong signal of "I no longer want this feature." The user **no longer receives coaching after dismiss**.  
- A "re-invitation" campaign (a separate product decision) can later make them eligible again — that entry point is follow-up.  
- Even if the user adds new photos, we do not auto-resume. Respect the user's dismiss intent first.

One-line summary (engineering suggestion, pending PM ratification):

**Dismiss \= full opt-out for MVP. No auto-resume on profile photo change. Re-invitation handled as a separate post-MVP product decision.**

**Risk if not decided.**

- "Show again after a short time" makes the user dismiss again, accumulating negative reactions.  
- Conversely, "show again if photos change after dismiss" contradicts the user's intended opt-out. \-\> We don’t know if they don’t like that insight or they are hoping to fully opting out from the 

**Why this matters in this session.** Dismiss semantics determine whether SOUP should suppress the user before calling AURA. The exact SOUP field name is not part of the AURA contract; the behavior is.

**Question for the room (product level only).**

1. Is "dismiss \= no more coaching" the right behavior, or should we re-show under some conditions? \-\> Show again (new coaching) when user changes their profile photo  
2. If the user adds/changes photos, should dismiss auto-clear? (Recommendation: do not clear) Yes  
3. If a re-invitation campaign becomes likely, who brings that decision and when? 

**Agreement (fill in during meeting).**

- Dismiss \= no more coaching afterward (Yes / other behavior): **Yes** *(engineering suggestion — pending PM ratification by Jaini/Juniper)*  
- Dismiss auto-clear on photo change (No / Yes / conditional): **No** *(engineering suggestion — pending PM ratification)*  
- Future re-invitation campaign owner / criteria: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ *(post-MVP product decision)*  
- Notes: `photo_review_opt_in` (boolean, default `true`) is a SOUP-internal reference shape for implementing this behavior, replacing the older `dismissed_at` timestamp shape per Evan 4/24 inline comment \+ Brandon 4/28 confirmation. The exact field name is not part of the AURA contract.
