## 5\. Track B — Required Engineering Decisions

Audience: SOUP backend, AURA/MGAI engineers, Client/Surface engineering.

Take [§3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.15m0x797spk8)'s inputs as-is and freeze the contract and implementation boundary. Once these 6 items close, both sides can start mock/integration.

### 5.1 B1 — SOUP → AURA single endpoint

**Severity**: P0 (the zero point of engineering work)

**What we're deciding.** What endpoint surface SOUP and AURA agree on so that both teams can begin parallel implementation. Specifically, whether to freeze a single POST /v1/photo-review and keep AURA stateless, vs. building auxiliary status/result/cancel endpoints. We also decide that "ready/read state" is **outside the AURA API contract**.

**Recommendation.**

- Endpoint freezes as **POST /v1/photo-review only**.  
- AURA remains a stateless generation service. We do not build product-state endpoints like status / result / cancel / dismiss / viewed.  
- Read/state behavior for displaying results to the user or surfacing them in the next session is a SOUP / Client product-surface concern and is out of scope for the SOUP → AURA contract. Concretely, AURA does not own:  
  - **read**: Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper can read ready coaching from SOUP-owned product state.  
  - **ready state**: SOUP can expose whether a generated coaching result is ready, not yet viewed, and still valid for the current photo-set signal.  
  - **marking state**: Client can mark viewed / dismissed / clicked so SOUP can suppress or re-surface the right UI later.

API surface organized by layer:

| Layer | API | Required | Owner | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| SOUP → AURA | POST /v1/photo-review | Required | AURA/MGAI | Frozen in this session |
| SOUP internal | photo-change-signal-keyed result store/lookup (placeholder `profile_version`) | Required | SOUP | Invalidate on photo change (mechanism TBD with SOUP), hard ceiling 30 days |
| SOUP → AURA | GET /v1/photo-review/{id} | Not built | — | Only needed if AURA becomes an async job service |
| SOUP → AURA | cancel / delete | Not built | — | Unnecessary if AURA does not store results |

**Risk if not decided.**

- SOUP cannot start mock or integration work.  
- AURA cannot lock request validation and response schema.  
- Contract mismatches surface in QA/E2E right before launch.

**Why this matters in this session.** SOUP and AURA need to run parallel implementation. If contract isn't frozen, both have to assume — and contract mismatches found late are the most expensive.

**Question for the room.**

1. Can SOUP start mock/integration on the POST /v1/photo-review contract immediately?  
2. Do you agree to the boundary that AURA provides only a stateless generation API?

**Agreement (fill in during meeting).**

- Freeze single endpoint (Yes / change): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Agree AURA stateless (Yes / No): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

### 5.2 B2 \+ B3 — Request field hydration and photo path format

**Severity**: P0 (mock/contract dependency)

**What we're deciding.** Which fields are carried directly in the SOUP → AURA request, which fields AURA hydrates through `user-gateway`, and which single photo S3 reference format is used. Without this split, SOUP may over-build a large payload while AURA simultaneously plans to hydrate the same data. Conversely, if hydration access slips, AURA cannot validate or run the request.

**Recommendation.**

**Note (4/28)**: `profile_version` is **SOUP-internal only** and intentionally **not** sent in the AURA request. Per Brandon/Evan/Trideep agreement in the 4/28 kick-off, SOUP only invokes AURA when the user's *photos* have changed; AURA does not need a freshness key in-band. `profile_version` is only a placeholder for SOUP's internal photo-change signal (see [§5.5 B6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.r1xgqe953h07) and [§5.6 B7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.g9cgep2lrbzv)).

**Hydration direction (4/28 — Brandon, surfacing Evan's 4/24 inline comment)**: the old field list is the **maximal** request shape. If AURA can onboard `user-gateway` access for hydration, the SOUP→AURA payload should slim down to a lookup key plus only the fields that genuinely cannot be hydrated from `user-gateway`. AURA-side `user-gateway` access feasibility is the gating question — confirmed feasible on 4/28 (Brandon: "as long as we have a means to access the information"). This section now freezes the **boundary to discuss**, not a blindly maximal payload.

Hydration / request boundary to confirm:

| Field | Proposed source | Reason / decision needed |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| request\_id | SOUP request | tracing, idempotency, debugging |
| user\_id | SOUP request | minimal lookup key for AURA-side `user-gateway` hydration |
| age | Prefer AURA hydration from `user-gateway`; SOUP request fallback if access is not ready | segment matching, prompt context |
| gender | Prefer AURA hydration from `user-gateway`; SOUP request fallback if access is not ready | segment matching, prompt context |
| country\_code | Prefer AURA hydration from `user-gateway`; SOUP request fallback if access is not ready | region / language / eligibility context; confirm source of truth |
| interests | Prefer AURA hydration from `user-gateway`; SOUP request fallback if access is not ready | personalized photo suggestion |
| bio | Prefer AURA hydration from `user-gateway`; SOUP request fallback if access is not ready | coaching behavior depends on whether bio exists |
| photos | Prefer AURA hydration from `user-gateway` if it can return the current ordered photo set and read paths; otherwise SOUP request | primary input |
| photos\[\].id | Request or hydrated with photos | response photo reference, repetitive identification |
| photos\[\].s3\_path | Shared decision: request if `user-gateway` cannot reliably provide read paths; otherwise hydrate with photos | source image read path; format still needs to be canonical |

Photo S3 reference format:

- **Default: full S3 path** (single `s3_path` string per photo). Aligns with photo-touchup and other prior MGAI photo-related projects (Trideep, 4/24 inline comment).  
- Do not accept bucket \+ s3\_key in parallel — single canonical format only.

For P1 optional fields and naming policy, see [Appendix A](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.onhhl06qfu33).

**Risk if not decided.**

- SOUP sends a maximal payload while AURA also builds hydration, creating duplicated work and mismatched sources of truth.  
- AURA assumes `user-gateway` hydration is available, but integration starts before access / fields are ready.  
- Photo path format drifts across SOUP, AURA, and prior photo-touchup conventions.

**Why this matters in this session.** Mock work depends on the request boundary. We need to agree which fields are request payload vs. AURA-hydrated so SOUP and AURA can build in parallel without duplicating hydration work.

**Question for the room.**

1. Which fields will AURA hydrate from `user-gateway`, and which fields must remain in the SOUP request for MVP?  
2. Is `user_id` the only required lookup key for hydration, or does AURA need additional SOUP-provided identifiers?  
3. Confirmed: full S3 path (`s3_path`) if photo paths are sent in the request. If hydrated, can `user-gateway` provide the same canonical read path?

**Agreement (fill in during meeting).**

- Request payload fields: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- AURA-hydrated fields via `user-gateway`: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Photo path format / source: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

### 5.3 B4 — SOUP owns the trigger gate

**Severity**: P0 (where Track A decisions live as code)

**What we're deciding.** Where the gate that decides "do we call AURA?" lives, and how it splits between SOUP and AURA. The gate has two stages — (a) deterministic conditions decidable from input data alone, owned by SOUP, and (b) conditions that require LLM judgement on the actual photos (e.g., "are the photos diverse enough"), evaluated by AURA at inference time. Without this split, SOUP tries to imitate the LLM domain and the boundary breaks; AURA gets exposed to product state and responsibilities mix.

**Recommendation — two-stage gate.**

**Stage 1: SOUP-side deterministic gate** (judgeable from input data alone).

```
App open
  → SOUP: check experiment / region / feature-gate eligibility
  → SOUP: check user is still eligible after dismiss policy ([§3.5 A6])
  → SOUP: check photo freshness and debounce/coalescing semantics ([§5.5 B6])
  → SOUP: apply the one-calendar-day cooldown internally ([§3.1 A1+A3])
  → Only when all conditions pass: SOUP → AURA POST /v1/photo-review
```

The implementation fields behind these checks are SOUP-internal. `photo_review_opt_in`, `last_generated_at`, and `profile_version` appear elsewhere only as reference shapes, not as SOUP → AURA contract fields.

**Stage 2: AURA-side LLM-derived gate** (judgeable only by looking at the photos).

```
AURA receives POST /v1/photo-review
  → AURA: prompt + Gemini call (evaluate user photos)
  → LLM judgment: this user is already diverse / non-repetitive → status="skip", fill skip_reason
  → Otherwise: status="success" + 5-element coaching response (post-4/28: bottom_sheet_title/body, coach_title/body, repetitive_clusters)
  → SOUP: store in cache or record generation_skipped event based on response status
```

So among the [§3.3 A4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.q4iaelimp80o) skip conditions, "high diversity / low repetitiveness" is judged by AURA, not SOUP. The rest is SOUP's call.

**Risk if not decided.**

- If SOUP imitates the LLM domain (diversity/repetition judgment), accuracy drops and product criteria scatter.  
- If AURA holds product state (dismiss, last-generated-date, etc.), deletion/retention responsibility flows into the inference layer.  
- Without a skip branch in the response, SOUP misreads "LLM-judged skip" as a normal success and stores wrongly in cache.  
- Mismatched timing between SOUP's deterministic gate and AURA endpoint availability slips launch.

**Why this matters in this session.** The two-stage gate is the place Track A decisions take code form. Without locking it, both teams keep guessing about boundary.

**Question for the room.**

1. Do SOUP/MGAI agree to the structure where AURA judges "this user is already diverse / non-repetitive" via LLM at inference time and returns status="skip"?  
2. Is status="skip" \+ skip\_reason the only non-visible LLM-derived control signal AURA returns in MVP? (Recommendation: yes; visible rendering data such as `repetitive_clusters[]` stays in [§3.2 A2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg).)  
3. ~~Does SOUP already have profile/photo change detection?~~ **Answered (Evan, 4/24 inline comment): Needs to be built — no existing infra.** This is not an AURA contract blocker, but SOUP should confirm the photo-freshness / debounce follow-up owner async.

**Agreement (fill in during meeting).**

- Agree two-stage gate (SOUP deterministic \+ AURA LLM-derived) (Yes / change): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- AURA-derived skip signal shape: status="skip" \+ skip\_reason / other: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Photo-freshness / debounce follow-up owner: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

### 5.4 B5 — SOUP-owned product-state reference

**Severity**: Reference only (not a SOUP → AURA contract blocker)

**What this is.** A reference map for how SOUP may implement product state. This section does **not** decide SOUP's internal field names, physical storage, or client-facing APIs. The SOUP → AURA contract is simply: AURA does not receive or own product-state fields such as `photo_review_opt_in`, `last_generated_at`, viewed/dismissed/clicked state, or surface exposure history.

**Reference.**

| Area | Owner | Contract status |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Product state for eligibility / dismissal / viewed state / exposure history | SOUP / Product backend | SOUP-internal; not sent to AURA |
| Possible dismiss implementation reference: `photo_review_opt_in` default `true`, set `false` on dismiss | SOUP / Product backend | Reference only; exact field name is SOUP-internal |
| Possible one-calendar-day cooldown implementation reference: `last_generated_at` or equivalent generation history | SOUP / Product backend | Reference only; exact field name is SOUP-internal |
| Photo-change signal / cache key component (previous placeholder `profile_version`) | SOUP / Product backend | Reference only; mechanism TBD by SOUP; see [§5.5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.r1xgqe953h07) |
| Inference metadata: prompt version, model name/config, Gemini latency/status/error, inference output payload, inference logs | AURA / MGAI | AURA-owned metadata returned/logged through the agreed API contract |

**Explicit dismiss handling reference.** Per [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm), MVP behavior under discussion is "dismiss \= no more coaching." SOUP can implement that with `photo_review_opt_in` or another internal representation. AURA should only see eligible requests.

**Risk if misunderstood.**

- The shared session spends time on internal SOUP field naming instead of the SOUP → AURA API contract.  
- AURA accidentally treats SOUP product-state fields as request or response requirements.

**Why this is included.** It gives AURA enough context to understand why SOUP may or may not call POST /v1/photo-review. It is not a decision item unless SOUP proposes sending any of these fields to AURA.

**Question for the room.** None expected. Discuss only if SOUP proposes sending one of these product-state fields to AURA.

### 5.5 B6 — Photo freshness events and debounce

**Severity**: P0 (shared ground for trigger eligibility, cache invalidation, dedupe, idempotency)

**What we're deciding.** Which photo events count as a "fresh photo set" and how SOUP should debounce or coalesce event bursts so one user action sequence does not trigger duplicate AURA calls. The exact SOUP-internal field or mechanism (event listener, hash, monotonic version, etc.) remains a SOUP implementation detail. The shared-session question is the **semantics**: photo-only invalidation, same-day cooldown, and event debounce behavior.

**Note on terminology** (4/28 update): throughout this doc the placeholder `profile_version` refers to *whatever SOUP-internal mechanism* tracks photo-set changes. SOUP confirmed they have **no existing `profile_version` infrastructure** (Evan, 4/24 inline comment; Henry, 4/24 inline comment "i've also not heard of profile\_version"). The exact mechanism — event-based (listening to photo CRUD events on user-gateway), photo-set hash, monotonic version increment, or other — is a **SOUP-internal implementation detail TBD with the SOUP team**. This does **not** block the SOUP↔AURA contract or AURA-side development kickoff: `profile_version` does not appear in the SOUP→AURA request or response, so AURA can build against the contract while SOUP picks the mechanism in parallel.

**Recommendation.**

- `profile_version` (placeholder name for whatever signal SOUP picks) is a **SOUP-internal photo-change signal** derived only from SOUP-available photo state — it is not part of the AURA request or response payload. Prompt version and model name are **not** inputs to this signal.  
- The trigger set is **photo-only** for MVP — non-photo profile changes (bio / prompt / interest / descriptor) do **not** invalidate the cache. Reason (Evan, 4/24 inline comment): keying invalidation off non-photo edits would burn AURA cost any time a user updates a bio/prompt without changing photos, which has no information lift for photo coaching.  
  - photo add  
  - photo delete  
  - photo replace  
- SOUP should debounce / coalesce photo-change events before deciding whether to call AURA. The open engineering question is the debounce window and event grouping rule, for example:  
  - multiple add/delete/replace events in one edit session should produce at most one fresh photo-set signal.  
  - repeated saves that end with the same ordered photo set should not create duplicate generation.  
  - if a user changes photos multiple times before the next eligible app-open / next calendar day, SOUP should generate against the latest photo set only.  
- Photo reorder, bio/prompt/interest/descriptor edits, and core fields (age/gender/country/relationship intent) are **not** in the MVP trigger set. If product wants any of these to count later, PM brings a separate decision.

**Risk if not decided.**

- Stale coaching might be exposed against an updated profile.  
- No way to prevent duplicate generation against the same photo-edit burst.  
- Even with a photo-change-signal-keyed cache, no invalidation criterion means stale results pile up.

**Why this matters in this session.** AURA does not need the actual freshness key, but both sides need the same invalidation and debounce semantics. If non-photo edits unexpectedly invalidate the cache, AURA cost rises. If photo events are not debounced, one user editing photos can produce redundant AURA calls or stale generation against an intermediate photo set.

**Question for the room.**

1. Do SOUP/MGAI agree that MVP freshness is photo-only: photo add / delete / replace?  
2. Do SOUP/MGAI agree that reorder, bio, prompt, interests, descriptors, age, gender, country, and relationship intent do not invalidate MVP Photo Review coaching?  
3. What debounce / coalescing rule should SOUP use for photo-change events before calling AURA?  
4. Confirmed context: SOUP has no existing `profile_version` concept; mechanism choice is SOUP-internal and can proceed async without blocking AURA contract work.

**Agreement (fill in during meeting).**

- MVP freshness event set: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Non-photo edits do not invalidate cache (Yes / change): \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Photo-change debounce / coalescing rule: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- SOUP-internal mechanism follow-up owner: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

### 5.6 B7 — Persistence: photo-change-signal-keyed cache

**Severity**: P0 (UX vs. backend design fork)

**What we're deciding.** Cache semantics, cache key shape, and retention/legal review owner. Implementing the [§3.1 A1+A3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) product decision ("keep same coaching when photos do not change, new coaching next day when they do") directly produces a cache that is valid while the SOUP-internal photo-change signal stays the same, not one that expires by time. This section does **not** require the shared session to choose Redis vs. DynamoDB vs. another SOUP storage technology.

**Recommendation.**

- Implement a **photo-change-signal-keyed cache** in SOUP. The same cache entry keeps getting reused as long as the photo set is unchanged. Strict ephemeral is not adopted.  
- Cache key semantics \= (user\_id, SOUP-internal photo-change signal, prompt\_version, model\_name). Same as the dedupe key ([§6.6 B10](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.b6k1csktdmh3)). The photo-change signal is derived only from SOUP-side photo state; `prompt_version` and `model_name` are separate AURA/MGAI version dimensions.  
- Hard ceiling starts at \~30 days as a retention/legal hypothesis. The ceiling is for storage hygiene, not invalidation.  
- Cache and exposure state are owned by SOUP / product backend ([§5.4 B5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.rk2a2g52g598)).  
- AURA response includes prompt\_version and model\_name so SOUP can construct the cache key. SOUP attaches its own internal photo-change signal (`profile_version` placeholder — see [§5.5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.r1xgqe953h07) note on terminology) when persisting; AURA does not see this value.  
- User-driven cache invalidation is photo-set change only. Prompt/model rollout is a separate system-driven cache miss / regeneration condition: if `prompt_version` or `model_name` changes, the old cached coaching no longer matches the current AURA inference config even when the user's photos are unchanged.  
- "No same-day new generation" is handled by the day-boundary / debounce check in *generation* ([§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915)), not by the photo-change signal itself.  
- Storage implementation: SOUP-internal follow-up. Evan confirmed (4/24 inline comment) that SOUP would not reuse current data-layer infra for this cache; choosing Redis / DynamoDB / other is not a shared AURA contract decision.

**Risk if not decided.**

- If cache key semantics conflate photo freshness with prompt/model rollout, SOUP may either miss required regeneration after an AURA change or over-trigger based on non-photo user edits.  
- Retention/legal review landing right before launch is a schedule risk.

**Why this matters in this session.** The cache semantics are the implementation form of A1+A3. With B6 freshness semantics in place, the shared decision is "what makes a cached result valid": user-driven invalidation is photo-set change, while system-driven invalidation comes from AURA/MGAI prompt or model version changes. Physical storage choice can move to SOUP async.

**Question for the room.**

1. Do SOUP/MGAI agree the photo-change signal is derived only from SOUP-side photo state, not from AURA/MGAI `prompt_version` or `model_name`?  
2. Do SOUP/MGAI agree user-driven cache invalidation is photo-set change only — photo add / delete / replace — while reorder and non-photo profile edits do not invalidate coaching?  
3. Do SOUP/MGAI agree `prompt_version` / `model_name` changes are separate system-driven regeneration triggers because the cached output no longer matches the current inference config?  
4. Should prompt/model rollout regeneration bypass the 1-calendar-day cooldown, or wait until the next eligible app-open?  
5. How far has retention/legal review progressed, and who owns the next round?

**Agreement (fill in during meeting).**

- Cache semantics / key shape: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Prompt/model rollout regeneration rule: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- SOUP storage implementation: SOUP-internal async follow-up  
- Retention/legal review owner / due: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_  
- Notes: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

## 6\. Optional / Follow-up (if time remains)

Once [§3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.15m0x797spk8) and [§5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.v7w1qmlfbg0z) close, SOUP and AURA can start mock/integration. The items below are (a) not launch-blocking, (b) decidable inside engineering, or (c) follow-up async. If time remains, close one or two; otherwise just set owner and due date.

### 6.1 A7 — Stability of response key naming

**Context.** Verify whether the [§3.2 A2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) backend response fields (bottom\_sheet\_title, bottom\_sheet\_body, coach\_title, coach\_body, per\_photo\_problems) remain stable post-launch.

**Recommendation.** If PM/Content guarantees that Figma copy/surface names won't shake for at least 6 months post-launch, use the field names above as-is. If stability is weak, start with generalized keys (hook\_title, hook\_body, coach\_title, coach\_body, photo\_problems) so the schema doesn't move with product copy. Owner: PM \+ Content, follow-up async.

### 6.2 A9 — Tie-breaker metric

**Context.** Who decides the representative photo within a repetitive photo cluster. Not an MVP blocker, but the tie-breaker should be consistent.

**Recommendation.** **Hybrid** — use a universal photo-quality metric when one exists, fall back to LLM visual judgment otherwise. Once metric coverage is wide enough, follow-up can unify it.

### 6.3 A10 — Analytics event taxonomy

**Context.** Tracking user behavior post-launch requires a frozen event taxonomy.

**Recommendation.** Freeze 5 categories (Generation lifecycle / Surface impression / Bottom sheet / Profile change / Failure-skip) as baseline. Per-category event details in the [Appendix Analytics](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.qzu97hagv42f). Attach common dimensions where available (request\_id, user\_id, SOUP-internal photo\_change\_signal, prompt\_version, model\_name, experiment\_arm, surface, session\_id). This session agrees only on the category structure; PM \+ Analytics close per-event additions/adjustments async.

### 6.4 B8 — Timeout and late result

**Context.** Gemini sync p99 is around 30.5 seconds, so timeouts happen even in normal operation.

**Recommendation.** SOUP→AURA timeout \= **30 seconds**. Late results arriving after timeout flow into the [§5.6 B7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.g9cgep2lrbzv) cache and are used in the next surface/session. Timeout/failure are recorded as observability events. Detail in [Appendix F.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.o67513q9a6mf). Engineering can decide internally.

### 6.5 B9 — Retry budget

**Context.** Retry raises success rate but increases cost and latency together.

**Recommendation.** **Single in-AURA transient retry** within a 30-second budget. SOUP does not re-call the same request and keeps the idempotency key. Retry-induced cost is reported as a separate item in cost estimates. Detail in [Appendix F.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.5rhxxhtme801).

### 6.6 B10 — Idempotency / dedupe

**Context.** Handling tracing and dedupe with a single request\_id causes incidents where retry breaks dedupe.

**Recommendation.** Split the keys. **request\_id is for tracing/idempotency only** (issued by SOUP). **generation\_key \= (user\_id, SOUP-internal photo-change signal, prompt\_version, model\_name) is for SOUP-internal dedupe only** — `profile_version` is only a placeholder for the SOUP-internal photo-change signal ([see §5.5 note on terminology](?tab=t.mxjwzzdcxg#bookmark=id.4zgifm3d34wa)); prompt/model values are separate AURA/MGAI version dimensions, not inputs to the photo-change signal. If an in-flight request exists with the same dedupe key, no new Gemini call is started; retries keep the same two keys. Detail in [Appendix F.3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.y4480sj9ljwm).

### 6.7 B11 — Response shape

**Context.** Final schema is closed by the post-4/28 simplification described in [§3.2.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.6ip59ri0fi4n) and [§3.2.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.40bkz0jhc7gi). `per_photo_problems` is dropped; `repetitive_clusters` is the single source of truth for the per-photo ℹ️ indicator.

**Recommendation.** Return the 5 Figma elements \+ skip branch in a single call:

- Always included: request\_id, status (success/skip), prompt\_name, prompt\_version, model\_name.  
- For status="success": bottom\_sheet\_title, bottom\_sheet\_body, coach\_title, coach\_body, repetitive\_clusters (array of `{cluster_id, kept_photo_id, flagged_photo_ids[], cluster_label}`; array order \= severity, worst first; empty array \= no per-photo ℹ️ shown).  
- For status="skip": skip\_reason required, the 5 elements omitted.

Sample in [Appendix A.5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.ehozon1a1qok). Naming stability decided in [§6.1 A7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.c19rdsusi8hi).

### 6.8 B12 — Observability

**Context.** Product event taxonomy (A10) and backend metrics are separated.

**Recommendation.** Product events are the 5 categories frozen in [§6.3 A10](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.j607oxyxzrxc). Backend metrics: request count / success / timeout / failure (reason) / Gemini latency distribution (p50/p90/p95/p99) / token count (input/output) / prompt\_version / model\_name. Detail in [Appendix F.4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.co4wq0usvswn).

### 6.9 B13 — Cost / latency source consistency

**Context.** A comment noted that latency was measured on gemini-3.1-flash-lite-preview while cost's underlying model is unclear.

**Recommendation.** Separately label sources for sync latency / batch dry-run / per-call cost / retry-adjusted effective cost. Cost is not in LP-606's decision frame; it stays as reference material. Detail in [Appendix G](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.xw65wziu9mgy).

### 6.10 A11 — Backfill timeframe

**Context.** The Apr 27 Spec Kick-off note posed *"Do we need to plan for any backfill timeframe with this feature?"* without an answer recorded.

**Options.**

- **No backfill** (default assumption) — at launch, only cold-start users gradually receive coaching. Engineering Docs estimate cold-start ramp-down at \~21 days.  
- **Day-1 backfill** — single batch generation for all eligible users right before/after launch. Requires Option 1 (batch) infrastructure, conflicting with LP-606's Option 2 single-path assumption.  
- **Targeted backfill** — accelerate cold-start only for a specific segment (e.g., 6+ photos & low diversity). Possible with Option 2 \+ a one-off external batch call.

**Recommendation.** **No backfill (keep default assumption)**. The 21-day cold-start ramp-down is short enough to gather post-launch data, and Day-1 backfill breaks the Option 2 single-path assumption. If post-launch Profile Home view rate is low, revisit Targeted backfill as a follow-up.

If the meeting decides differently, add a backfill path to the [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) trigger gate and add pre-fill logic to the [§5.6 B7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.g9cgep2lrbzv) cache.

## 7\. Appendices

### A. API Contract Detail

#### A.1 Reference endpoint

POST /v1/photo-review. Single boundary for SOUP calling AURA. Used for both request-time and background generation paths under Option 2 On-demand Sync.

#### A.2 Request field hydration boundary

Same as [§5.2 B2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.ju3zuxfeh321): freeze which fields remain in the SOUP request, which fields AURA hydrates from `user-gateway`, and which canonical photo path format is used.

#### A.3 P1 optional request fields

| Field | Status | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| target\_gender | Optional | multi-gender supported, array |
| city | Optional | prompt context. Not an MVP blocker |
| job\_titles | Optional | array |
| employers | Optional | array |
| schools | Optional | array |
| languages | Optional | multi-language follow-up |
| anthem | Optional | personalization fuel |
| lifestyles | Optional | personalization fuel |
| basics | Optional | personalization fuel |
| relationship\_intent | Optional | future tone/personalization |
| photos\[\].smartphoto\_score | TBD | tie-breaker candidate. coverage issues |

#### A.4 Request field decisions

| Decision | Proposal |
| :---- | :---- |
| country\_code | Fixed 2-letter ISO code |
| target\_gender | Fixed array |
| job/company/school | Fixed array |
| numeric enum vs string | Even if SOUP sends numeric enum, AURA/ML layer maps to LLM-friendly string |
| photo path | full S3 path default (`s3_path`), aligned with photo-touchup convention. Do not accept multiple formats simultaneously |
| prompt/model metadata | Always include prompt\_version, prompt\_name, model\_name in response and log |

#### A.5 Response shape candidate (Figma 5-element \+ LLM skip branch, post-4/28)

Figma displays information in the order bottom sheet (title/body) → "Review" button → Edit Photos screen (coach title/body \+ repetitive-cluster ℹ️ indicators). The backend response returns these 5 elements together in one call; if AURA judges the user is already diverse/non-repetitive, it returns an empty coaching via the status="skip" branch ([§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915)).

**A. status="success" — normal coaching response (post-4/28 simplified shape — see [§3.2.1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.6ip59ri0fi4n))**

```json
{
  "request_id": "71639584-1234-5678-9012-345678901234",
  "status": "success",
  "model_name": "gemini/gemini-3.1-pro-preview",
  "prompt_name": "photo-coaching-2026-03-17",
  "prompt_version": "v4",
  "bottom_sheet_title": "We have profile improvement tips",
  "bottom_sheet_body": "Adding a bit more variety to your photos can lead to more match opportunities",
  "coach_title": "Vary your photo angles more",
  "coach_body": "Your photos are mostly **selfies**. Adding a **full-body shot** or an **outdoor photo** gives users a more dimensional impression.",
  "repetitive_clusters": [
    {
      "cluster_id": "c1",
      "kept_photo_id": "abc-123",
      "flagged_photo_ids": ["def-456", "ghi-789"],
      "cluster_label": "repetitive mirror selfies"
    }
  ]
}
```

If no repetitive cluster exists, `repetitive_clusters` is `[]` and no per-photo ℹ️ is rendered; the user still sees `coach_title` / `coach_body` for general advice.

**B. status="skip" — LLM judges "no coaching needed"**

```json
{
  "request_id": "71639584-1234-5678-9012-345678901234",
  "status": "skip",
  "skip_reason": "already_diverse",
  "model_name": "gemini/gemini-3.1-pro-preview",
  "prompt_name": "photo-coaching-2026-03-17",
  "prompt_version": "v4"
}
```

When status="skip", the 5 element fields are empty or omitted. SOUP does not store in cache and records a coaching\_generation\_skipped event (skip\_reason=already\_diverse).

Open questions:

- The 5 element names above are candidates that map 1:1 to Figma. Naming stability is decided in [§6.1 A7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.c19rdsusi8hi).  
- ~~`per_photo_problems` shape decision~~ — resolved by dropping the array entirely (post-4/28).  
- Additional LLM-derived metadata candidates (severity, cta\_label, recommended\_swap\_photo, overall\_score) remain MVP-excluded — see [§3.2.3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.m5tvplya6ieb). Replacement guidance may appear in general coaching copy, but per-photo ℹ️ markers are derived only from `repetitive_clusters[]`.  
- skip\_reason enum starts with hypotheses like already\_diverse, low\_repetitiveness, insufficient\_input.  
- If localization is handled in the backend, the response shape changes to a localization-key form.

### B. Option 2 Flow

#### B.1 Base flow

**Day N — session in which coaching is generated:**

1. The user opens the app.  
2. SOUP-side deterministic gate ([§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) Stage 1\) checks eligibility.  
3. If the user is no longer eligible after dismiss policy, if the photo set has not changed, or if the one-calendar-day cooldown still blocks generation, do not call.  
4. Otherwise SOUP calls AURA via POST /v1/photo-review.  
5. AURA receives profile/photo/context and runs a Gemini sync call.  
6. AURA-side LLM-derived gate ([§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) Stage 2): if LLM judges "already diverse / non-repetitive," returns status="skip" \+ skip\_reason; otherwise returns status="success" \+ 5 elements (post-4/28).  
7. SOUP stores the result in the photo-change-signal-keyed cache when status="success" (hard ceiling 30 days). On status="skip", no cache and a coaching\_generation\_skipped event is recorded.  
8. If the user reaches a persistent surface like Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper within the session, ready coaching appears there. **The bottom sheet is not shown in this session.**  
9. On timeout or failure, no coaching is shown in this session.

**If the user takes a photo action in Day N:** current coaching and repetitive-photo markers are removed for that session and the surface falls back to default/success state. SOUP does not immediately re-call AURA from that action. The next eligible app open is the first refresh opportunity.

**Day N+1 onward — next app open:**

10. The user opens the app again.  
11. SOUP checks for cache hit (assuming the SOUP-internal photo-change signal has not changed).  
12. If a coaching with cache ready exists and the user remains eligible under SOUP's product-state checks, **the bottom sheet appears as a nudge at app open**.  
13. When the user taps the bottom sheet, they navigate to the Edit Photos screen and see coach\_title / coach\_body / repetitive-cluster-driven per-photo ℹ️ indicators.  
14. On dismiss, engineering suggestion (pending PM ratification): eligibility is removed per [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm).

### C. Ownership Model

| Component | Recommended ownership |
| :---- | :---- |
| Client | rendering and visible surfaces |
| SOUP backend | eligibility, product state, profile/photo context hydration, exposure history, day-boundary check, AURA invocation |
| AURA / MGAI | prompt/model/version management, prompt assembly, Gemini call, structured response generation, model/prompt metadata, inference logs |
| Storage / cache | product state and persisted coaching cache on SOUP/product backend; AURA may use only short-lived inference-local cache if needed |

### D. Persistence Choices (reference)

#### D.1 Strict ephemeral

No storage. Conflicts with the [§3.1 A1+A3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) decision ("keep same coaching when photos do not change"), so not adopted.

#### D.2 On-demand \+ photo-change-signal-keyed cache (adopted)

Reuse the same cache entry while the user's photo set is unchanged. Satisfies both cost savings and user-experience consistency. Set only a hard ceiling (e.g., 30 days) for retention. "No same-day new generation" is handled by the day-boundary / debounce check in the [§5.3 B4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.hloeoei51915) trigger gate, not cache.

#### D.3 Hybrid later

Precompute cache or batch path is follow-up. Out of LP-606 scope.

### E. Bottom sheet timing — risks and mitigations

Per the [§3.2](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) decision, the bottom sheet is shown **only at the next app open** (Evan \+ Jaini agreement, 4/24\~25). The remaining risks and mitigations under this policy are summarized below.

| Risk | Mitigation |
| :---- | :---- |
| If the user does not visit Profile Home / Edit Photos / Photo Cropper in the same session, no coaching is shown that session | The next-app-open bottom sheet pulls the user back. The first opportunity yields to surfaces; the second is guaranteed by the bottom sheet |
| Bottom sheet appears too often, causing user fatigue | Engineering suggestion (pending PM ratification): once dismissed, eligibility is removed per [§3.5 A6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.fd1j1miryyvm). If PM adopts a lifetime max-insights cap, treat it as a SOUP eligibility condition in [§3.3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.q4iaelimp80o), not bottom-sheet UX. |
| User receives it abruptly without prior notice | Review introduction copy / onboarding. Add opt-out if needed |
| Cache is stale at bottom sheet exposure (photos changed in the meantime) | The SOUP-side photo-change signal (placeholder `profile_version`) invalidates the cache on change. After invalidation, new generation the next day |
| Coaching generated on Day N, user did not visit the surface, and Day N+1 app open shows the bottom sheet directly — risk of feeling like an ad | Use bottom sheet copy in a referential tone like "a tip prepared in your previous session". Bottom-sheet visual treatment ([§3.2.4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.2cphljq6gksq)) should avoid implying a new scan happened in the current session |

### F. Reliability and Observability Detail

#### F.1 Timeout

p99 is around 30.5 seconds, so design around a 30-second budget. Late results after timeout flow into the [§5.6 B7](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.g9cgep2lrbzv) cache and are used in the next surface/session. Timeout/failure are recorded as observability events.

#### F.2 Retry

- SOUP does not re-call the same request.  
- Single in-AURA transient retry within a 30-second budget.  
- Retry count, backoff, and timeout budget explicit.

#### F.3 Idempotency / dedupe

- request\_id: tracing and idempotency  
- SOUP-internal dedupe key: (user\_id, SOUP-internal photo-change signal, prompt\_version, model\_name) — `profile_version` is only the placeholder for whatever photo-change signal SOUP picks ([see §5.5 note on terminology](?tab=t.mxjwzzdcxg#bookmark=id.4zgifm3d34wa)); prompt/model values are separate AURA/MGAI version dimensions, not inputs to the photo-change signal. The dedupe key lives entirely on the SOUP side and is not part of the AURA request/response.  
- If the same dedupe key is in-flight, no new Gemini call is started. Retry keeps the same key.

#### F.4 MVP observability set

See [Analytics Event Taxonomy Detail](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.mgcphs7lx54y).

### G. Cost and Latency Inputs

#### G.1 Known numbers

| Metric | Value | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| sync p50 | \~17.5 s | Gemini Flash-Lite sync call |
| sync p95 | \~25 s | Gemini Flash-Lite sync call |
| sync p99 | \~30.5 s | Drives timeout budget |
| test region Option 2 upper bound | \~$66K/month | Varies with trigger rate assumption |
| global Option 2 upper bound | \~$325K/month | Global run rate. Separated from experiment cost |
| batch dry-run observed median | \~16.8 min | Gemini 2.5 batch dry-run. Option 1 reference |

#### G.2 Open issue

The following must be labeled separately.

- Which model/config is sync latency measured on?  
- Which model/config is the batch dry-run on?  
- Which model/pricing/discount is per-call cost on?  
- What is the retry-included effective cost?

In the LP-606 decision frame, cost is not used as a decision item (reference material).

### Analytics Event Taxonomy Detail

| Category | Event | Emit owner | Meaning / measurement goal |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Generation lifecycle | coaching\_generation\_requested | SOUP | Just before AURA call after trigger gate passes |
| Generation lifecycle | coaching\_generation\_succeeded | AURA | Gemini call success, response returned |
| Generation lifecycle | coaching\_generation\_failed | AURA | Includes failure reason |
| Generation lifecycle | coaching\_generation\_skipped | SOUP | skip\_reason (same\_day\_already\_generated / photos\_unchanged / ineligible / dismissed) |
| Surface impression | coaching\_ready | SOUP | Result is exposable to the client |
| Surface impression | coaching\_ready\_but\_not\_viewed | Client | Not exposed by session end |
| Surface impression | coaching\_viewed | Client | Actually shown on a persistent surface |
| Surface impression | coaching\_clicked | Client | viewed → CTA or detail entry |
| Surface impression | coaching\_dismissed | Client | Dismissed on a persistent surface |
| Surface impression | coaching\_feedback\_submitted | Client | Optional feedback sheet response after dismiss; option list is Product/Design follow-up |
| Bottom sheet | bottom\_sheet\_impression | Client | Hook message shown |
| Bottom sheet | bottom\_sheet\_tap\_through | Client | Hook → detail entry |
| Bottom sheet | bottom\_sheet\_dismissed | Client | Bottom sheet itself dismissed |
| Bottom sheet | swipe\_drop\_off\_post\_impression | Client | Guardrail |
| Bottom sheet | session\_length\_post\_impression | Client | Guardrail |
| Profile change | profile\_edited\_after\_coaching | Client/SOUP | Change within N minutes after coaching exposure |
| Profile change | photo\_added\_after\_coaching | SOUP | Photo add event attribution |
| Profile change | photo\_removed\_after\_coaching | SOUP | Photo remove event attribution |
| Failure / skip | eligibility\_check\_result | SOUP | Gate pass/fail reason |
| Failure / skip | experiment\_arm\_assigned | Client/SOUP | Control vs treatment allocation |

Common dimensions (attached where available): request\_id, user\_id, SOUP-internal photo\_change\_signal, prompt\_version, model\_name, experiment\_arm, surface, session\_id.

### H. Option 1 related Out-of-scope items

Not directly addressed in the LP-606 Option 2 kick-off.

| Topic | Reason for separation |
| :---- | :---- |
| How SOUP gathers an hourly batch eligible user list | Option 1 batch architecture only |
| How many users/photos are processed in the hourly batch | Option 1 capacity planning only |
| Source of 17-min batch turnaround | Source needs to be specified in Option 1 decision doc |
| Whether SOUP must build new eligible-user-list infra | Big impact on Option 1 LOE |

### I. Comment Coverage

All comments on the Serving Options doc are reproduced verbatim, with links to where each is resolved (or classified as follow-up) in this doc. Grouped by topic, not chronology. Status: ✅ directly answered in this doc / 🟡 deferred to follow-up / 🔵 separated to a different track (e.g., Option 1 only).

#### I.1 Trigger frequency / per-app-open call ✅

*"Joining the party late so sorry if I am missing context... What is the reasoning for triggering this on every app open? Won't we waste compute on users who don't change their photos or already received coaching?"* — **Evan Keys, 4/24 1:52 AM**

*"I have similar question in a comment below.. 'should this be each app open or each app open AND any changes to the input i.e. new upload, deletions or replacement of their photo.?' @[trideep.rath@gotinder.com](mailto:trideep.rath@gotinder.com) and I talked about the latter which I added to the product spec."* — **Jaini Shah, 4/24 2:07 AM**

*"should this be each app open or each app open and any changes to the input i.e. new upload, deletions or replacement of their photo.?"* — **Jaini Shah, 4/23 5:27 AM**

**Resolution:** [§3.1 A1+A3](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.dya98ug2b1db) (keep same coaching if photos unchanged, new coaching the next day if photos change) · [§3.3 A4](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.q4iaelimp80o) (SOUP/AURA skip criteria) · [§3.4 A5](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.upygd9ysc76a) (app open as single trigger).

#### I.2 Same-session nudge vs next app open ✅

*"Why do we need to nudge the user in the same session we trigger coaching generation for option 2? I think users are nudged/disrupted enough mid swipe so adding another I think is a risk. It should be feasible to save state that is read on next app open giving an experience similar to option 1."* — **Evan Keys, 4/24 1:56 AM**

*"agree. I don't think we need to nudge them in the same session. The way i was thinking about the user experience is that once the coaching is ready, it shows up in the persistent surface areas (i.e. profile home, edit photos, photo cropper) and then at next app open is when the bottom sheet could show up. I believe this is similar to what growth opted for as well and also this approach makes sense with engagement team as well."* — **Jaini Shah, 4/25 3:49 AM**

*"if the user skips the nudge or skips viewing this coaching, would it be available to them the next app open? curious about session length per user and possibility of a user missing this (apart from disruptiveness causing them to miss this coaching moment). @[kevin.celustka@gotinder.com](mailto:kevin.celustka@gotinder.com) wdyt? cc: @[juniper.han@match.com](mailto:juniper.han@match.com) @[trideep.rath@gotinder.com](mailto:trideep.rath@gotinder.com)"* — **Jaini Shah, 4/23 4:35 AM**

*"Possible in theory, but it has to be orchestrated from backend. Basically some state saving logic has to be incorporated by backend. App open \--\> Is user eligible and has not seen feedback \--\> feedback service \--\> Feedback saved \--\> Bottom sheet displayed"* — **Trideep Rath, 4/23 6:12 AM**

*"can't it be surfaced and ready for them to access in the next session (if they are returning and no profile change)?"* — **Jaini Shah, 4/23 4:41 AM**

*"Yes \- Bottom sheet nudge cc: @[nancy.wu@gotinder.com](mailto:nancy.wu@gotinder.com)"* — **Jaini Shah, 4/23 5:26 AM**

**Resolution:** [§2 Exec Summary conclusion 6](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.k0j6n3y84wj8) · [§3.2 What we're deciding](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.8ftt94n6rzg) (Day N: persistent surfaces, Day N+1: bottom sheet) · [Appendix B](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.koy3dw3emuv5) (Day N \+ Day N+1 flow) · [Appendix E](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?ouid=101263465154277962712#heading=h.mvszifhvz0zr) (next-app-open policy risks/mitigations).

#### I.3 Cache / state ownership (ML vs backend) ✅

*"Cache should exist on the backend and not on the ml side."* — **Trideep Rath, 4/23 7:49 AM**

*"Is Aura a ML/LLM orchestration layer? If so I think related data should stay encapsulated in that layer. I recommend if we maintain state, that's a product/domain entity and that should be handled by SOUP team."* — **Evan Keys, 4/24 2:18 AM**

*"Why does ML own the coaching store ?"* — **Trideep Rath, 4/23 7:52 AM**

1\. 30-Minute Session Guide  
The reading order of the doc is the meeting order.

| Order | Section | Time | Goal |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | [§2 Executive Summary](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.k0j6n3y84wj8) | 3 min | Agree on the recommendation paragraph and the decision-result paragraph. Yes/no on "the big-picture direction is correct" |
| 2 | [§3 Track A — Required Product Decisions](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.15m0x797spk8) | 12 min | Close A1+A3, A2, A4, A5, A6 in sequence |
| 3 | [§4 Hand-off Map](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.do682u62dlny) | 3 min | Confirm what Track A outputs feed into Track B |
| 4 | [§5 Track B — Required Engineering Decisions](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.v7w1qmlfbg0z) | 10 min | Close B1, B2/B3, B4, B5, B6, B7 in sequence |
| 5 | [§6 Optional / Follow-up](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U/edit?tab=t.h0gjhkoyvzcu#bookmark=id.s7bybr323135) | Remainder | A7, A9, A10, A11 (backfill), B8–B13. If time runs short, set owner and due date and defer to async |

Every decision item uses the same box format.

What we're deciding. State the decision question in a plain paragraph that every stakeholder can understand at once.   
Recommendation. The recommended option and its rationale.   
Risk if not decided. What concrete work gets blocked if we defer.   
Why this matters in this session. (Secondary) Why we must close it here. Read only if the urgency is unclear from the three items above.   
Question for the room. One or two sharp questions to drop in the meeting.   
Agreement (fill in during meeting). Capture the agreed outcome on the spot.  
2\. Executive Summary  
Stakeholder discussion has already settled the serving direction as Option 2 (On-demand Sync). The goal of this kick-off is not to finish the entire backend design but to enable SOUP backend and AURA/MGAI to run parallel implementation through next quarter. To do that, this session handles two things at once: (1) the items product must answer before engineering starts and (2) the items engineering must freeze in the contract once those answers land.

Recommendation paragraph (product view):

Photo Review shows new coaching the next day when the user changes a photo or profile, and keeps the prior coaching when nothing changes. Coaching is generated at app open, but within that session it appears only on persistent surfaces (Profile Home, Edit Photos, Photo Cropper). The bottom sheet appears as a nudge on the next app open, and tapping it opens the Edit Photos screen with the coach title/body, problematic photo identification, and per-photo problem descriptions. Dismissing it stops further coaching.

Unpacked, this becomes the following 8 conclusions.

1. The SOUP → AURA contract freezes as a single endpoint, POST /v1/photo-review. We do not build auxiliary endpoints like status/result/cancel.  
2. The trigger entry point is app open only. SOUP checks whether the user is a skip target, whether photos have changed since the last coaching, and whether photos changed on the same day. Profile Home / Edit Photos are result-display surfaces, not triggers.

Update on 4/27: Yes, the trigger is app-open only.

- Important note: The bottom sheet however, will be triggered in the next app open so that the user will get the bottom sheet alert right when they enter the app, not mid swipe.

For post D0,

- The users who have dismissed the previous coaching will not be eligible for a new coaching until they make a change to their profile photo.  
- The users who made some sort of change to their profile photo will get the new coaching after some length of cool down. 

3. Same coaching when photos do not change; new coaching the next day when they do. SOUP owns product state (viewed, dismissed\_at, last\_generated\_at, profile\_version, surface exposure history) and the cached coaching.  
4. AURA owns the inference boundary as well as prompt/model versioning. That is, prompt/model versioning, prompt assembly, the Gemini call, structured response, prompt/model metadata, and the inference log are all AURA's responsibility.  
5. Persistence is a profile\_version-keyed cache on the SOUP side. The same cache entry keeps getting reused as long as the profile is unchanged. We set a hard ceiling (e.g., 30 days) for retention. Strict ephemeral is not adopted.  
6. The bottom sheet appears only on the next app open, not in the same session (Evan \+ Jaini agreement, 2026-04-24\~25). In the same session, coaching is shown only on persistent surfaces (Profile Home, Edit Photos, Photo Cropper); the bottom sheet appears as a nudge at the next app open. The backend response returns 6 elements together in a single call — bottom\_sheet\_title / bottom\_sheet\_body, coach\_title / coach\_body, and photo-level problematic\_photo\_ids / per\_photo\_problems. The elements themselves are exactly as in Figma; only the exposure timing of the bottom sheet shifts to the next session.  
7. Dismiss is not a short-term block but permanent removal from eligibility (a re-invitation campaign is a separate follow-up).

Update on 4/27: No, this is not a permanent removal from feature eligibility. The user will get a new coaching message if they make changes to their profile photo. Theoretically, if they do not change their profile photo ever, they will not be eligible for a new coaching message.

8. Retry is not a SOUP re-call but a single in-AURA transient retry within a 30-second budget. The dedupe key is (user\_id, profile\_version, prompt\_version, model\_name).

Deliberate delta from Engineering Docs (this is the v2 follow-up). The original [Photo Review MVP Engineering Docs](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Q4x0DwGJuDGjTaqFAtlbHFH-KD1cWZosPI-zdhFTQ9U) defined Option 2 as "Ephemeral. No stored inferences", and the Coaching Store was specified as Option 1 only (MGAI-owned). This doc adds a profile\_version-keyed cache on the SOUP side so that (a) the same coaching is preserved for users whose photos have not changed and (b) the result can be displayed in the next session. This change must be agreed in the kick-off. Also, per the Apr 22 Status Update doc decision, "Custom ML-model based approach will not be included in MVP Photo Review" — i.e., the self-hosted GPU step is dropped from MVP and AURA calls Gemini directly.
